This means you have until December 31, 2021 to spend FSA money earmarked for last year. The extension also applies for your 2021 FSA money - the credit will be available until the end of 2022. </p><p>We recommend checking your plan details to ensure you&#39;re making the most of your money.</p><p>If you still have FSA bucks to spend, consider <a href=\"https://www.pjatr.com/t/TUJGR0lOSEJGSEhLR01CR0ZNRUVG?url=https%3A%2F%2Ffsastore.com%2F%3Futm_source%3Dpepperjam%26utm_medium%3Daffiliates%26utm_campaign%3D133628%26clickId%3D3368631638\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored\">FSAstore.com</a>. FSAstore.com has thousands of items that are guaranteed to be covered by your FSA. Below, we answer frequently asked questions about FSA dollars, and how you can avoid letting your money go to waste.</p><bi-shortcode id=\"table-of-contents-sticky\" class=\"mceNonEditable\" data-type=\"h2\">Table of Contents: Masthead Sticky</bi-shortcode><p> </p><h2><strong>What is FSA?</strong></h2><p>Many employers offer access to Flexible Spending Accounts, which let you put away pre-tax dollars for eligible healthcare products and services (think everything from surgery and medical bills to thermometers and first-aid kits). Storing money in an FSA account is a great deal, provided you spend it before the deadline.</p><h2>How does FSA work?</h2><p>FSA operates on a use-it-or-lose-it provision; you must spend the money in your FSA account by the end of the year or risk losing it for good. Typically, you&#39;d either have to spend it all by a deadline (either December 31 or March 15) or roll a portion of it over. </p><p>The COVID relief bill signed late last year changes things, though. </p><p>Now, you have an extra year to spend your FSA dollars, for both 2020 and 2021. Put plainly: the FSA money you accrued in 2020 will still be available to you until December 31, 2021; the money you accrue in 20201 will be available until December 31, 2022.</p><p>FSA Store estimates that <a href=\"https://fsastore.com/About/About-FSA-Store-PressReleases.aspx\">more than $400 million is forfeited every year</a> in FSA funds because employees either miss or forget their spending deadlines (based on estimates using data from the 2017 FSA and HSA Consumer Research conducted by VISA). It&#39;s your money and it&#39;s pre-tax - it doesn&#39;t make sense not to use it.</p><h2><strong>What can you buy with your FSA money?</strong></h2><p>You can use FSA dollars to pay for medical expenses that aren&#39;t covered by a health plan, like co-pays, deductibles, dental and vision care, or dependent daycare, though eligible expenses can vary based on the plan. But if it&#39;s nearing the end of the year and you haven&#39;t used your money to help meet your deductible or pay medical expenses, you have the option of spending it on supplies like over-the-counter medication.</p><p>The nitty-gritty details depend on the plan your employer has in place, but you can skip the burden of research by shopping the selection at the <a href=\"https://www.pjatr.com/t/TUJGR0lOSEJGSEhLR01CR0ZNRUVG?url=https%3A%2F%2Ffsastore.com%2F%3Futm_source%3Dpepperjam%26utm_medium%3Daffiliates%26utm_campaign%3D133628%26clickId%3D3368635414\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">FSA store</a>. They do the homework for you and curate more than 4,000 products that are guaranteed to be covered. If they&#39;re somehow not, you get your money back. </p><bi-shortcode id=\"commerce-link\" class=\"mceNonEditable\" data-cardtype=\"medium\" data-pid=\"606dc1513d35010018fe11c1\" removed","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/austin-russell-replaces-kylie-jenner-youngest-self-made-billionaire-forbes-list-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img class=\"copyright\">Luminar</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Austin Russell was the youngest self-made billionaire on Forbes&#39; annual World&#39;s Billionaires List.</li>\n<li>The 26-year-old runs a company that provides the technology for self-driving cars.</li>\n<li>Russell replaced Kylie Jenner as the youngest self-made billionaire after she was removed in 2020.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>26-year-old Austin Russell became the world&#39;s youngest self-made billionaire on <a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/sites/arielshapiro/2021/04/06/the-worlds-youngest-billionaires-2021-include-a-teenager-from-germany-a-crytpo-magnate-and-a-stanford-dropout/?sh=2562136a509d\">Forbes&#39; annual World&#39;s Billionaires List</a> when it was released on Tuesday. </p><p>Russell <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/luminar-elon-musk-austin-russell-lidar-volvo-cars-2020-10\">became a billionaire virtually overnight</a> after his company Luminar Technologies was listed on the Nasdaq via a SPAC merger in December. Forbes currently estimates Russell&#39;s net worth at $2.4 billion. </p><p>Russell received a $100,000 fellowship from billionaire investor Peter Thiel in 2012 and dropped out of Stanford to found Luminar Technologies. The company builds sensors for autonomous vehicles.  </p><p>The company&#39;s sensors have been used to create self-driving cars at companies like Volvo and Toyota. Luminar&#39;s technology relies on LIDAR, a process that uses pulses of light to create a 3-D map of a car&#39;s environment. The technology allows self-driving cars to determine the best course of action and avoid obstacles on the road.</p><p>In 2019, Tesla CEO <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/luminar-elon-musk-austin-russell-lidar-volvo-cars-2020-10\">Elon Musk spoke out against the technology, calling it &#34;doomed.&#34;</a> Instead of lidar, which has become popular with numerous automotive companies, including Alphabet&#39;s self-driving start-up Waymo, Tesla relies on external cameras for its &#34;Full Self-Driving&#34; software.</p><p>Russell replaced 23-year-old Kylie Jenner on the list after <a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/sites/chasewithorn/2020/05/29/inside-kylie-jennerss-web-of-lies-and-why-shes-no-longer-a-billionaire/?sh=37a4666425f7\">Forbes&#39; removed her in 2020, </a>saying the beauty guru&#39;s net worth had been overvalued in the documents provided to them by Jenner.</p><p>At the time, Jenner responded to Forbes decision to remove her from the list via her Twitter account.</p><p>&#34;What am I even waking up to,&#34; she <a href=\"https://twitter.com/KylieJenner/status/1266396922752843779\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"7f94766b962d42851ad232c6314f72d0\">wrote in a tweet</a>. &#34;I thought this was a reputable site.. all I see are a number of inaccurate statements and unproven assumptions lol. I&#39;ve never asked for any title or tried to lie my way there EVER. Period.&#34;</p><p>When Jenner was put on the cover of Forbes in 2018 it <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/kylie-jenner-self-made-billionaire-forbes-cover-sparks-backlash-2018-7\">sparked backlash, as some readers questioned whether she was truly &#34;self-made&#34;</a> due to her family&#39;s wealth.</p><p>The executive is one of four self-made billionaires on Forbes&#39; list that are in their 20s. The other young billionaires include the founders of DoorDash Andy Fang and Stanley Tang, as well as crypto investor Sam Bankman-Fried. All four billionaires are new additions to Forbes&#39; list.</p><p>The billionaire list saw several new developments this year as COVID-19 shook up the economy. In 2020, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/trump-drops-forbes-billionaires-list-2021-4-1030278939\">former President Donald Trump dropped 298 spots on the ranking</a>. Bloomberg estimates <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/donald-trump-net-worth-down-700-million-since-becoming-president-2021-3?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\">Trump&#39;s net worth plunged $700 million during his presidency.</a></p><p>The youngest billionaire on the list was <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/worlds-youngest-billionaire-teenager-in-germany-forbes-2021-4\">18-year-old Kevin David Lehmann, a German drugstore heir worth $3.3 billion.</a></p><p><em><a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/sites/arielshapiro/2021/04/06/the-worlds-youngest-billionaires-2021-include-a-teenager-from-germany-a-crytpo-magnate-and-a-stanford-dropout/?sh=2562136a509d\">Read the full list on Forbes&#39; site.</a></em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/0TPGSvVJn2E\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 07 Apr 2021 17:10:44 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/606dbe3f30004b0019b26626?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"019ee77aab7139b74444bfb824a73f32","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn13@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-37-48-158_c28a1aeefd7707fd.webp","destWidth":2222,"destHeight":1666,"sourceBytes":110640,"destBytes":110640,"author":"gkay@businessinsider.com (Grace Kay)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/606dbe3f30004b0019b26626?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn13@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-37-48-158_c28a1aeefd7707fd.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn8@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-38-29-454_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=0TPGSvVJn2E:VjlB32knuG0:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn24@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-38-25-325_ba4dbe3af1fa4e31.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=0TPGSvVJn2E:VjlB32knuG0:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn47@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-28-389_7d4924f81de6dbe2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn15@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-27-264_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=0TPGSvVJn2E:VjlB32knuG0:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn79@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-30-120_cf965f0960d12367.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/0TPGSvVJn2E":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn71@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-23-696_4df169bce4142b2f.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617817067362},{"createdTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:47","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:47","title":"Derek Chauvin's trial is testing the stress levels of Black Americans. Here's what leaders and allies can do to help.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/chauvin-trial-stress-black-americans-how-leaders-allies-can-help-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606b4198a7d803001963ec07?format=jpeg\" alt=\"george floyd derek chauvin trial protests\" height=\"1666\" width=\"2222\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>People gather the day before jury selection for Derek Chauvin, the former police officer charged in the death of George Floyd, in Minneapolis in March.\n<p class=\"copyright\">REUTERS/Leah Millis</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Psychologists tell Insider that Black employees may feel afraid to speak up about their experiences.</li>\n<li>Managers should reach out to Black employees and encourage them to prioritize their mental health.</li>\n<li>There are also steps Black professionals can take to preserve their wellbeing and alleviate stress.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>On a recent lunch break, Dion Bullock watched the trial of Derek Chauvin, the former Minneapolis police officer charged in the death of George Floyd. </p><p>Bullock&#39;s body tightened as he listened to a 9-year-old witness describe Floyd&#39;s struggle as Chauvin knelt on his neck. &#34;I felt angry that a child had to relive the trauma of that day and have her testimony dissected publicly,&#34; he said.</p><p>Then he heard an electronic ping; he was needed on a client call. He turned on his laptop&#39;s camera, and his smiling colleagues, chatting about the weather, greeted him. &#34;I grappled with the tension in that moment: Do I share the pain I am feeling from watching the trial or do I compartmentalize it?&#34; </p><p>Bullock, who works at <a href=\"https://workbravely.com/\">Bravely</a>, a career-coaching company, recognizes the dark and profound irony of his emotions. His job involves helping organizations build more equitable workspaces. &#34;How do I process this as a person? How do I help other Black people process it? And how can I help allies and white people?&#34; he said. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606b402ea7d803001963ec02?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Dion Bullock\" height=\"809\" width=\"1080\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Dion Bullock, the equity, inclusion, and belonging strategy lead at professional counseling company Bravely, discussed the emotional labor of trying to concentrate on work during the trial.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Dion Bullock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><a href=\"https://www.thelancet.com/journals/lancet/article/PIIS0140-6736(18)31130-9/fulltext\">Research</a> has found that police killings of Black American men, including Freddie Gray, Michael Brown, and Eric Garner, can take an enormous toll on Black people&#39;s mental health. And after a year in which racial tension and political unrest gripped the nation and a pandemic disproportionately harmed Black and brown communities, the Chauvin murder trial is severely testing their stress levels. </p><p>Psychologists tell Insider that Black people might feel afraid to speak up in the workplace about what they&#39;re going through, for fear of retaliation. Against the backdrop of a murder trial that&#39;s seen as a referendum on racial justice, these highly charged emotions have important and far-reaching implications for managers, allies, and Black employees. </p><p>&#34;You already feel like a target and that the work environment is not a safe place,&#34; said Danielle Spearman-Camblard, a Connecticut-based psychologist and therapist who specializes in racial trauma.&#34;When a trial like this is affecting your emotional health and job performance, you feel like you can&#39;t go to your supervisor without risking a slap on the hand. You put up and shut up and go into survival mode.&#34;</p><h2>What Black professionals are feeling right now</h2><p>Watching or reading about the Chauvin murder trial, a veritable weekslong narrative of a traumatic event, is triggering for many Black people. In psychology, the effect is known as vicarious or secondary trauma, which is caused by exposure to survivors who have been traumatized themselves. This kind of trauma is associated with <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/what-is-burnout\">burnout</a>, emotional exhaustion, and lower levels of accomplishment, Farah Harris, a psychotherapist based in Illinois, told Insider. </p><p>&#34;There are layers of trauma Black Americans have to grapple with,&#34; Harris said.</p><p>The effects of intergenerational or historical trauma - trauma that a cultural or racial ethnic group experiences related to events or institutions that oppress that group, such as enslavement - compound the pain, she said.</p><p>Juggling the psychological weight of the trial with work obligations - catching up on coverage during a midmorning coffee break and viewing fragments of testimony between Zoom meetings - creates a sense of dissonance. Emotions are raw, and people feel fragile.</p><p>Briana Young, an MRI and CT technologist based in Georgia, said she can bear to watch the trial only in short clips at a time. Even then, she feels her blood pressure rise. </p><p>&#34;I&#39;m angry,&#34; she said. &#34;It&#39;s like watching a trainwreck. Derek Chauvin is a white supremacist who looked at George Floyd as less than human. It&#39;s infuriating.&#34; </p><p>Normally after her 40-minute drive to work, she spends a minute or two practicing deep breathing and meditation to help center herself and focus on the workday ahead. Now, during the Chauvin trial, she spends twice the time meditating. </p><p>&#34;I desensitize through meditation,&#34; she said. &#34;That&#39;s the only way I can continue to function without continuing to function in anger.&#34; </p><p>André Blackman, the founder and CEO of North Carolina-based Onboard Health, an executive recruiting firm focused on inclusivity in healthcare, echoed the sentiment. &#34;There are moments throughout the day where I look at the headlines to get a sense of how things are progressing,&#34; he said. &#34;But there&#39;s an emotional toll if I check in constantly.&#34; </p><p>He describes his psychic state as a burning, low-grade frustration mixed with feelings of emotional numbness. He worries that Chauvin will not be convicted, despite the haunting video of Floyd&#39;s death. An acquittal would repeat a history of past outcomes in which a Black man is killed by police on camera and officers suffer no legal consequences. </p><p>&#34;I feel like this is the moment: Society will have a conscience, and justice will be served,&#34; Blackman said. &#34;But I&#39;ve been let down time and time again</p><h2><strong>Don&#39;t put the burden on Black employees</strong></h2><p>Black employees are in need of support from their organizations, said Tina Opie, an associate professor in the management division at Babson College. &#34;Let&#39;s not put the burden on Black employees to be the arbiters of their own sanity in the workplace. Let&#39;s instead put the responsibility and burden on white leaders to demonstrate empathy for their workers and to put in place systems and processes that dismantle systemic racism.&#34;</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">-Dr. Tina Opie  (@DrTinaOpie) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1376572249029873665?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">March 29, 2021</a></blockquote><script async=\"\" src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p> </p><p>Managers need to open lines of communication with their employees and make clear that they care about their team members&#39; emotional and social well-being. They should also encourage workers to take a mental-health day and also say explicitly that they will not face penalties for asking for temporary reprieve from their workload. </p><p>In an ideal world, managers know to &#34;extend grace and empathy,&#34; toward Black employees, but workers might have to explicitly ask for compassion. &#34;Say, &#39;This is tough. I need to either disconnect or pause regular work for a little bit.&#39;&#34; </p><p>Most importantly, Opie said, managers must not put Black employees in the position of having to serve as a resource to help others in the organization understand the trial as a teachable moment.  &#34;Don&#39;t request anything extra from them,&#34; she said. </p><p>Educate yourself on your own, Beverly Tatum, a nationally recognized scholar and author of multiple books on race in America, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-white-colleagues-can-be-allies-to-their-black-coworkers-2020-6\">told Insider</a>. Order books on the topic, watch documentaries, and read <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/essays-and-works-of-journalism-by-black-authors-on-racism-2020-6\">first-person accounts and essays</a> from Black writers.</p><p><a href=\"http://workingwelldaily.com/\"></a>Harris recommends <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-white-colleagues-can-be-allies-to-their-black-coworkers-2020-6\">allies</a> check in on Black colleagues but only if they have a close relationship. Otherwise, outreach could come off as offensive. &#34;You want to avoid performative allyship,&#34; she said, referring to instances in which allies, often white allies, want to be seen as a good person.  </p><p>Harris recommends language along the lines of: &#34;Hey I wanted to see how you were doing given everything going on with Chauvin&#39;s trial. Don&#39;t worry about responding to this message. Focus on your own well-being, but know I&#39;m here to talk.&#34; </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a reveal how Fed authorities view the path to economic recovery and the potential for inflation.</li>\n<li>The 10-year Treasury yield is holding steady at 1.67% after climbing above 1.7% last month.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/10-things-opening-bell\">Sign up here for our daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell</a></li>\n</ul><p>US stocks trade mixed Wednesday as investors anticipate the <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/economic-calendar?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\">minutes from the Federal Reserve&#39;s March policy meeting</a> to be <a href=\"https://www.federalreserve.gov/newsevents/calendar.htm#:~:text=Publication%20date%20for%20this%20release,1%3A00%20p.m.\">published at 2 p.m. ET</a>. Details will reveal how central bank authorities view the path to economic recovery in the country as well as how they may handle inflation.</p><p>The US economy has rebounded faster than what most have expected due in large part to President Joe Biden&#39;s landmark $1.9 trillion stimulus package paired with steady vaccine rollout throughout the country, which has helped the labor, manufacturing, and travel sectors recover. The President on Tuesday <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/biden-to-announce-us-adults-eligible-covid-vaccine-april-19-2021-4\">moved up the timeline</a> for all American adults to be eligible for a COVID-19 vaccine to April 19 from May 1. </p><p>The 10-year Treasury yield has held steady at 1.67% after climbing to the highest levels in over a year in March.</p><p>&#34;The fact that the bond yields barely changed last week despite a raft of strong economic numbers ... indicates that market has already gone a long way to pricing in the economic rebound,&#34; Kathy Jones, Charles Schwab chief fixed income strategist, said in a note. &#34;<u></u>Also, it is hard to see U.S. yields surge from here since they are so far above those in many other developed markets in both real and nominal terms. With the current wide yield spread, foreign investors should find U.S. yields attractive.&#34;</p><p>Mike Owens, sales trader at Saxo Markets, also said the Fed minutes might give better insight on how members envision the economic recovery and when they expect to hike rates.</p><p>&#34;If 5-year US Treasury yields break above 1%, they might provoke a squeeze that could send 10-year yields on a fast track to 2%,&#34; he said. </p><p>US shares <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/stock-market-wrap-volatility-archegos-meltdown-capital-dow-nasdaq-sp500-2021-4-1030278793\">closed lower Tuesday</a>, with the Dow Jones Industrial Average and S&#38;P 500 retreating from record highs reached the previous session. New sell-offs linked to the Archegos Management Capital crisis added to unease in markets even after US data revealed the economic rebound is on track.</p><p><strong>Here&#39;s where US indexes stood after the 9:30 a.m. ET open on Wednesday:</strong></p><ul><li><strong><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/s&p_500?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestedium=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">S&#38;P 500</a>:</strong> 4,073.73, down 0.01%</li><li><strong><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/dow_jones?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestm=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Dow Jones industrial average</a>:</strong> 33,414.55, down 0.05% (15.69 points)</li><li><strong><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/nasdaq_composite?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestm=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Nasdaq composite</a>: </strong>13,676.38, down 0.15%</li></ul><p>On Tuesday, The International Monetary Fund <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/economic-outlook-gdp-global-growth-vaccines-stimulus-recovery-uneven-imf-2021-4\">lifted its estimate for global gross domestic product growth</a> this year to 6% from 5.5%. The improvement was largely tied to expectations for economic reopening and mass vaccination, especially in advanced economies.</p><p>Oil prices climbed on optimistic economic data.</p><p><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/commodities/oil-price?type=wti?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestm=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">West Texas Intermediate crude</a> rose by 0.83% to $59.82 per barrel. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/commodities/oil-price?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestce=markets&#38;utm_medium=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Brent crude</a>, oil&#39;s international benchmark, was also up 0.78% to $63.23 per barrel. Oil prices dropped earlier in the week when the Organization of the Petroleum Exporting Countries, or OPEC, said that it will <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/oil-prices-today-wti-brent-barrel-demand-worries-opec-covid-2021-4-1030274667\">add about two million barrels of oil each day</a> to the market from May to July, easing production cuts. </p><p>Goldman Sachs CEO David Solomon meanwhile told <a href=\"https://twitter.com/SquawkCNBC/status/1379406482572259335\">CNBC Tuesday</a> that he expects <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/bitcoin-regulation-cryptocurrencies-goldman-sachs-ceo-predicts-big-evolution-2021-4-1030280731\">a major transformation</a> in how the US government regulates bitcoin and other digital assets. &#34;I think there&#39;ll be a big evolution as to how this evolves in the coming years,&#34; the CEO said. </p><p><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/btc-usd?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\">Bitcoin</a> slipped 3.42% to $56,612.61 as the rally stalls. Last week, the cryptocurrency <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/bitcoin-price-today-60000-renewed-institutional-backing-paypal-visa-cme-2021-3-1030265701\">flirted with the $60,000-level</a>.</p><p>The <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/coinbase-q1-revenue-jump-bitcoin-crypto-market-too-volatile-forecast-2021-4-1030280362\">revenue of Coinbase</a> soared more than 800% year-on-year in the first quarter of this year, the company <a href=\"https://investor.coinbase.com/news/news-details/2021/Coinbase-Announces-First-Quarter-2021-Estimated-Results-and-Full-Year-2021-Outlook/default.aspx\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">revealed</a> on Tuesday. But the cryptocurrency exchange said the market is still too volatile to provide solid financial forecasts. Coinbase is set to directly list on the Nasdaq exchange <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/coinbase-plans-direct-listing-2-weeks-crypto-exchange-go-public-2021-4?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">on April 14.</a></p><p><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/commodities/gold-price?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestm=ingest\">Gold</a> rose to 0.44% to $1,736.13 per ounce.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-market-today-fed-minutes-treasury-yields-dow-nasdaq-sp500'>Business height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 07 Apr 2021 16:24:48 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/606daf0f70954f0019195972?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"5d531adacf9b7ccb9ae105dd69ce0246","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn57@2020_5/2021/04/07/17-38-23-644_e21b50b659593502.webp","destWidth":3563,"destHeight":2672,"sourceBytes":560646,"destBytes":560646,"author":"ilee@insider.com Lee)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/606dae3d30004b0019b265dc?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn48@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-38-30-621_e4d13c790c4384c7.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn8@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-38-29-454_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=Z10w3CwrEW0:eYdJK56aW1o:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn31@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-26-928_4c40b50f251de79c.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=Z10w3CwrEW0:eYdJK56aW1o:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn32@2020_2/2021/04/07/17-38-25-204_5438914c7e7baced.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn15@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-27-264_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=Z10w3CwrEW0:eYdJK56aW1o:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn96@2020_2/2021/04/07/17-38-26-372_45eb9ccb9d72b5b6.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/Z10w3CwrEW0":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn76@2020_5/2021/04/07/17-38-24-509_1b2af7053632df73.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617817067375},{"createdTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:47","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:47","title":"How to get tickets to the Masters, and how much it costs to get into the world's second-most exclusive sporting event","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-get-tickets-masters-golf-tournament-2018-3","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606de36970954f0019195abd?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Masters Tournament Badges\" height=\"1667\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Patrons often wear all of their badges on their hats or shirts.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Andrew Redington/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li><strong>Masters tickets are considered the second-hardest to obtain in sports, trailing only the Super Bowl.</strong></li>\n<li><strong>Tickets are cheap if you are lucky enough to be a patron or win the annual lottery.</strong></li>\n<li><strong>If you don&#39;t get tickets directly from Augusta National, be prepared to spend thousands.</strong></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.insider.com/sports\">Visit Insider.com for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Want tickets - or badges - to the Masters? It&#39;s possible, but it is not easy unless you are willing to shell out the big bucks.</p><p>There are three ways to get in during Masters week: Patron badges, daily tournament tickets, and practice round tickets. Below we take a look at how to obtain all three.</p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\tPatron badges\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5abe957860b8d7ea0c8b4606?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Masters patrons with badges on their hats\" height=\"683\" width=\"1024\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">David Cannon/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Owning a patron badge is a lot like being a season-ticket holder for the Green Bay Packers, except more mysterious because nobody outside of Augusta National knows how many exist.</p><p>Once you have one, you can keep it for the rest of your life. You pay $375 each year, and you have access to the entire week at Augusta National for the Masters.</p><p>Children aged 8-16 can attend for free if they are with somebody with a patron badge. They do not have to be related.</p>\n\tThe waiting list for badges\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/57051f78910584e73c8bad38?format=jpeg\" alt=\"The Masters\" height=\"862\" width=\"1200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Andrew Redington/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>If a person who owns a patron badge dies, it can only be transferred to a surviving spouse. Other family members are not eligible. If there is no surviving spouse, the badge goes back into the pool and is awarded to somebody on the waiting list.</p><p>The patron waiting list is uber-exclusive. Augusta National first created it in 1972. It got so long that Augusta closed the list in 1978. It was briefly re-opened in 2000, and Augusta National has not opened it since.</p>\n\tThe secondary market for patron badges\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5caf451b89df3d1c7c2c4fb2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Masters patrons\" height=\"1134\" width=\"1800\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Chris O&#39;Meara/AP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The patron badges are typically available on the secondary market through ticket brokers or hospitality groups offering Masters packages. Sellers often put them up for sale daily, but that typically requires a sizeable deposit, and they must return the badge at the end of the day.</p><p>Tickets are limited in 2021 due to the ongoing pandemic. Badges for the 2019 tournament went for a minimum of $2,000 for the opening round and $9,000 for all four days.</p>\n\tDaily tournament tickets\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5caf457a65fe291a4a0d2c4b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Masters patrons at Augusta National\" height=\"668\" width=\"1024\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Augusta National/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Since 2012, Augusta National has offered a limited number of tickets to each round <a href=\"https://tickets.masters.com/en_US/index.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">through a lottery on their website</a>. The deadline for applying for the lottery is typically June 1 during the previous year, and only one application is allowed per address.</p><p>Tickets for the 2021 tournament went for $115 each, and applicants were limited to two per round.&#160;</p>\n\tPractice round tickets\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/4f7ca6b5eab8ea905400002a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"The Masters Par 3 Contest\" height=\"371\" width=\"660\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">ESPN</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Augusta National also offers tickets to the practice rounds on Monday, Tuesday, and Wednesday, <a href=\"https://tickets.masters.com/en_US/index.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">through the same lottery on their website</a>.</p><p>Tickets for the 2021 practice rounds went for $75 each, and applicants were limited to four tickets per practice round.</p>\n\tScalping tickets\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5caf4622b1e0a21b271e71ab?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Augusta National\" height=\"609\" width=\"1007\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Augusta National/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The big thing to remember when buying Masters tickets from scalpers is that it is against the law within 2,700 feet of Augusta National.</p><p>People will also often wait outside of Augusta and ask for tickets from people leaving the tournament. Because of this practice, Augusta National now limits each to three re-entries per round.</p>\n</div><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Gaines)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/606de36970954f0019195abd?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn11@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-24-157_02656508524a41a1.webp","https://i.insider.com/5abe957860b8d7ea0c8b4606?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn2@2020_1/2021/04/07/17-38-24-964_b7d55d92ca6fb095.webp","https://i.insider.com/57051f78910584e73c8bad38?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn47@2020_1/2021/04/07/17-38-29-608_d8eccaf6a91864b2.webp","https://i.insider.com/5caf451b89df3d1c7c2c4fb2?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn44@2020_5/2021/04/07/17-38-26-949_0475b4d4d3c3d05e.webp","https://i.insider.com/5caf457a65fe291a4a0d2c4b?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn28@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-25-405_8127c50ef8471817.webp","https://i.insider.com/4f7ca6b5eab8ea905400002a?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn96@2020_1/2021/04/07/17-38-27-634_6f45cfce84d397d1.webp","https://i.insider.com/5caf4622b1e0a21b271e71ab?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn55@2020_2/2021/04/07/17-38-27-016_234aa997011b537f.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn8@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-38-29-454_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=hhETDNmVQxY:-t-koGwEWKw:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn23@2020_5/2021/04/07/17-38-29-844_369134da6c432974.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=hhETDNmVQxY:-t-koGwEWKw:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn87@2020_2/2021/04/07/17-38-28-889_166f214de6a2a49d.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn15@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-27-264_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=hhETDNmVQxY:-t-koGwEWKw:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn56@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-26-174_291d65cfe754587e.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/hhETDNmVQxY":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn88@2020_1/2021/04/07/17-38-28-330_9df2524d4d46a901.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617817067368},{"createdTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:47","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:47","title":"5 ways to fix an Xbox One controller that is blinking or flashing","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/why-is-my-xbox-one-controller-blinking","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606dcb6d30004b0019b26664?format=jpeg\" alt=\"xbox one controller\" height=\"1249\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>There are a few ways you could troubleshoot your Xbox One controller if it&#39;s blinking.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>If your Xbox One controller is blinking, your controller may not be paired to your Xbox One.</li>\n<li>To stop your Xbox One controller from blinking, check that the controller isn&#39;t paired to another system and that it has enough battery.</li>\n<li aria-level=\"1\">You may need to pair your Xbox One controller by holding down the pair button or by connecting it with a micro USB cable to the console.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tech-reference\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Visit Insider&#39;s Tech Reference library for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>There are a number of reasons why your Xbox One controller may be blinking or flashing. But if you see the controller blinking, the Xbox One controller most likely has a pairing issue.</p><p>Here&#39;s how to troubleshoot issues with your Xbox One controller if it&#39;s blinking or flashing.  </p><h2>Make sure your Xbox One controller is paired and in range</h2><p>You might find that your Xbox One controller is blinking or flashing due to pairing issues. It may be paired to another console, be out of range of the console, or is attempting to be paired on a console that already has eight other paired controllers. </p><aside class=\"quick-tip headline-regular\"><p><strong>Quick tip:</strong> <a href=\"https://support.xbox.com/en-US/help/hardware-network/controller/wireless-controller-solution\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Xbox says</a> the range for wireless controllers is 19 to 28 feet, but if your gaming setup is around walls, facing away from you, in a cabinet, or might experience interference from other nearby wireless devices, consider decreasing your range. </p></aside><p>If the controller doesn&#39;t seem to be reacting to your console at all, it may be connected to another Bluetooth device or console. To pair your controller back to your Xbox console if it was the last device you paired it to, double-press the pair button to have it switch the connection back.  </p><p>You can also check how many paired controllers you have in the console&#39;s settings in the Accessories menu under Devices &#38; connections. Xbox One allows up to eight paired controllers, so if none are the one you&#39;re currently using, you&#39;ll need to sync one of the paired controllers to another device in order to free up a pairing slot. </p><h2>Pair your Xbox One controller to your console again</h2><p>To stop your Xbox One controller from blinking and pair it to your console, just press down on the pair button on your Xbox One console and then release it, and within 20 seconds, hold down the corresponding pair button on your controller.</p><p>The controller should flash more rapidly for a moment, then display a continuous light. When that happens, it&#39;s paired.</p><h2>Connect your Xbox One controller to your console with a micro USB cable</h2><bi-shortcode id=\"related-article-module\" class=\"mceNonEditable\" data-type=\"5d9cabb0591bb74c812a45f9\" data-title=\"How to connect a Xbox One controller to your Xbox One console, with or without a USB cable\" data-url=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-connect-xbox-one-controller\" data-thumbnail=\"https://i.insider.com/undefined\">Related Article Module: How to connect a Xbox One controller to your Xbox One console, with or without a USB cable</bi-shortcode><p>To get rid of the blinking light on your Xbox One controller, you can also pair it with your console by connecting it via a physical micro USB cable. </p><p>Though this may not be preferable when compared to a wireless connection, connecting your Xbox One controller to your console should resolve all issues. </p><h2>Check the batteries on your Xbox One controller</h2><p>The flashing light on your Xbox controller may be an indication that it has a low battery. </p><bi-shortcode id=\"related-article-module\" class=\"mceNonEditable\" data-type=\"5d9ce87ae8815b09662e0274\" data-title=\"Here are the best ways to charge your Xbox One controller\" data-url=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-charge-xbox-one-controller\" data-thumbnail=\"https://i.insider.com/undefined\">Related Article Module: Here are the best ways to charge your Xbox One controller</bi-shortcode><p>There are a couple of ways to charge your Xbox One controller&#39;s batteries. That includes using a Play &#38; Charge Kit, a micro USB cable, or a rechargeable battery pack. But you can also use standard AA batteries if those are what you have on hand. </p><p>If you know your batteries are fully charged and the light is still blinking, pop the batteries out, wait 15 seconds, and then put them back in to see if that fixes the issue. </p><h2>Restart your Xbox One console or update your controller</h2><p>If pairing your controller and checking the batteries doesn&#39;t work, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-restart-xbox-one\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">restart your Xbox One console</a> by holding the power button for 10 seconds. Turn it back on, then try again.</p><p>You should also consider <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-update-xbox-one-controller\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">updating the firmware on your controller</a>. While controllers made after June 2015 can update wirelessly, all Xbox One controllers can be updated using the USB cord that came with your console. </p><bi-shortcode id=\"related-article-module-end-of-article\" class=\"mceNonEditable\"> </bi-shortcode><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 01:37:47","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:47","title":"Warren Buffett's former deputy just published her first annual letter since quitting to build her own Berkshire Hathaway. Here are the 10 best quotes.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/warren-buffett-former-deputy-tracy-britt-cool-first-annual-letter-2021-4","description":"<p><strong><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606dcb6530004b0019b26663?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Tracy Britt Cool\" height=\"754\" width=\"1508\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Tracy Britt Cool.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jNah-2v2pP4\" target=\"_blank\">Fortune/YouTube</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></strong></p><ul><li><strong>Warren Buffett&#39;s protégée left Berkshire Hathaway to start her own company, Kanbrick.</strong></li><li><strong>Tracy Britt Cool and her cofounder published their first annual letter this week.</strong></li><li><strong>They underscored their long-term view and warned easy money is distorting markets.</strong></li><li><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</strong></li></ul><p>Warren Buffett&#39;s former deputy, who quit Berkshire Hathaway to build her own conglomerate last year, just published her <a href=\"https://mcusercontent.com/64e1b84729b4195a49b750934/files/469734a0-92b8-4d8d-985b-284fb0581a9c/Kanbrick_2020_Annual_Letter.pdf\">first annual letter</a>.</p><p>Tracy Britt Cool was hired as Buffett&#39;s financial assistant in 2009, went on to chair several Berkshire businesses, and served as CEO of another one, Pampered Chef. She partnered with her former CFO, Brian Humphrey, to found a long-term investment firm called Kanbrick last April.</p><p>Kanbrick closed its first deal last summer, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/warren-buffett-former-lieutenant-berkshire-hathaway-thirty-one-gifts-2020-7-1029402341\">securing a stake</a> in Thirty-One Gifts. It recently <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/warren-buffett-berkshire-hathaway-tracy-britt-cool-kanbrick-business-program-2021-1-1029960778\">rolled out</a> &#34;Build with Kanbrick,&#34; a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tracy-britt-cool-mentorship-program-warren-buffett-protege-2021-2\">three-month support program</a> for the bosses of mid-sized businesses.</p><p>Britt Cool and Humphrey&#39;s letter echoes Buffett&#39;s yearly missives to his investors over the past six decades. They clearly share the Berkshire chief&#39;s long-term focus, passion for educating others, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-write-like-warren-buffett-berkshire-hathaway-shareholder-letter-2021-3\">knack for entertaining readers</a>, and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/warren-buffett-warned-investors-stocks-speculation-annual-letter-lawrence-cunningham-2021-3\">willingness to sound the alarm</a> when needed.</p><h2>Here are the 10 best quotes from the letter, lightly edited and condensed for clarity:</h2><p>1. &#34;The name Kanbrick is a nod to our shared experience growing up in Kansas and our belief that great things are built &#39;brick by brick&#39; - day by day, little by little, through hard work, discipline, and integrity. This is in our DNA, and we lived this every day growing up and working in our family businesses - farming for Tracy and cabinetry for Brian.&#34;</p><p>2. &#34;Great companies are not built in spreadsheets, and we create value through building enduring companies vs financial wizardry and loads of debt.&#34;</p><p>3. &#34;We stay away from macro predictions like foreign exchange or interest rates - our Magic 8 ball hasn&#39;t been helpful, and, despite years of searching, we have yet to find a crystal ball.&#34;</p><p>4. &#34;Based on our research and personal experience, we believe the combination of Purpose, People, and Performance drives results. This three-legged stool is rarer than a four-leaf clover - most companies only focus on one or two areas and few deliver on all three.&#34;</p><p>5. &#34;If setting out on a 100-mile road trip, then you&#39;d want more than 100 miles&#39; worth of gas (especially if you&#39;re traveling through western Kansas where gas stations are rarer than cows).&#34; - <em>describing how they apply a &#34;margin of safety&#34; to their annual plan.</em></p><p>6. &#34;The crucible of capitalism craves efficiency - customers always want better products faster and at lower prices - and the dust heap of history is littered with formerly iconic firms such as Polaroid and Blockbuster. COVID is another reminder that we can&#39;t predict the next crisis; however, we know dark clouds and stormy seas will appear again in the future.&#34;</p><p>7. &#34;While many investors look to run a three-year sprint, we are running a marathon and are comfortable leaving some gas in the tank (and giving up some short-term gains) to ensure we can finish mile 26 strong.&#34;</p><p>8. &#34;Moats and sources of competitive advantage evolve and erode over time. Newspapers used to have an enviable moat, but we all see how the water there has dried up.&#34;</p><p>9. &#34;The current low-rate, high-stimulus environment seems to have distorted incentives and market signals.&#34; - <em>Kanbrick and Humphrey warned that the long-term impacts of government aid for ailing businesses are unclear, and cautioned that low interest rates are boosting asset prices and &#34;numbing investors to potential risks.&#34;</em></p><p>10. &#34;Eventually each business&#39; value must be anchored in the cash it produces.&#34;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the 01:37:47","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:47","title":"How I organically grew my Twitter following with just 30 minutes of daily use","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/organically-grow-twitter-following-with-these-tips-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/605399e6fe6a340019acf62d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"woman looking at phone texting at home\" height=\"1548\" width=\"2064\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A community-focused growth strategy is the best way to organically build a real following on Twitter.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Delmaine Donson/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Digital branding expert Jeremy Moser says he grew his Twitter following from 50 to over 2,500 in 30 days. </li>\n<li>He explains that posting too often but not engaging with other users can stall potential growth.</li>\n<li>Have a clear aim of which communities your content should reach and prioritize quality over quantity.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>I&#39;ve had a <a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/twitter\">Twitter</a> account since 2017. I hardly used it, and it amassed a grand total of 50 followers. </p><p>When I returned to Twitter, nobody was engaging with me. I was speaking into the void.</p><p>Within 30 days, I grew my following to 2,500+, gaining 2.5 million impressions with just 30 minutes of usage per day. </p><p>Here is how you can do the same. </p><h2>Community focus</h2><p><a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/article/312492\">Building a community</a> is the best way to grow an active, engaged, real following on Twitter.</p><p>Followers are just a number at the end of the day. Would you rather have 10,000 followers, but still struggle to drive action, or 500 followers on the edge of their seats awaiting your content? </p><p>Lead your strategy with a community focus.</p><p>In other words: not just tweeting and expecting the <a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/engagement\">engagement</a> to roll in. I flipped the script and started tweeting less, and engaging more. </p><p>I set a strict schedule to tweet two times per day of my best, most insightful work. Snippets from <a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/online-content\">online content</a> I wrote, tips on how I grew my <a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/business\">business</a>, lessons from being in the startup trenches. </p><p>You don&#39;t have to think of content ideas. Just be yourself and share your stories from real-life to business!</p><p>Once you have valuable content on your profile, start engaging in specific communities. </p><p>Do you want to tweet about startups? Don&#39;t follow startup companies, follow the employees of those companies. Then, look at who is replying, liking, and retweeting their content. </p><p>Engage with those people and build real relationships. </p><p>As you do this, those who you are engaging with will naturally click on your profile. When they see your valuable insights, they&#39;ll follow. </p><p>You&#39;ll quickly build a small community that supports your content as you support theirs. </p><h2>Utilize direct messages</h2><p>One of the most underrated aspects of Twitter is the DM functionality. </p><p>And no, it&#39;s nothing compared to <a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/linkedin\">LinkedIn</a>. No spam, and definitely no sales pitches. </p><p>Twitter is about unique, interesting, <a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/article/280701\">engaging content</a>. It&#39;s not about trying to make instant profits from a follower. </p><p>In direct messages, welcome new followers and ask them to talk about themselves. Learn about the projects they are working on and where you can help. </p><p>Doing so fosters a real bond and friendship. People engage with people who engage with them.</p><p>When growing a following, you have to understand that Tweeting is just a small portion of your strategy. </p><p>The biggest impacts for growing an engaged following happen in real conversations with people. </p><h2>Refine your content approach</h2><p>Content on Twitter has evolved dramatically from the early days of sharing your every random thought to insightful, detailed threads, one-liners that spark curiosity, and so much more. </p><p>The content you share on Twitter is a direct indicator to potential followers of how much <a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/value\">value </a>you can deliver for them. </p><p>Growth via better content requires retweets. Retweets expand your reach infinitely, opening your ideas to new audiences and driving action on your profile. </p><p>The best ways to elicit more retweets and engagement are: </p><ul><li>Create detailed threads: be contrarian and hook people in with a hot-take thread on a popular subject</li><li>Tap into relevant news</li><li>Mention users with an existing following (but avoid those with millions of followers)</li><li>Share numbers and success stories</li><li>Describe failures and lessons learned</li></ul><p>For example, I wrote a thread curating some of the best threads I&#39;ve seen on Twitter. It received over one million impressions and 59,000+ engagements. </p><p>The most interesting content isn&#39;t copied, faked, or forced. It&#39;s from real experiences. Share yours and people will naturally gravitate. </p><p>Lastly, always remember: Twitter is about making friends and creating a like-minded community. </p><p>Be friendly, be supportive, and have fun with it. </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/organically-grow-twitter-following-with-these-tips-2021-4'>Business Insider</a></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=lp0Y13YFlv4:xC7RNvgUGK8:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606dae7730004b0019b265dd?format=jpeg\" alt=\"stimulus checks\" height=\"512\" width=\"1024\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Economic stimulus checks are prepared for printing at the Philadelphia Financial Center May 8, 2008 in Philadelphia, Pennsylvania.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a fulfills Biden&#39;s goal to send 150 million payments in his first 100 days in office just 77 days in.</li>\n<li>The IRS plans to send checks for non-filers in the Veterans Affairs database next week.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The Biden administration has cleared its goal of delivering more than 150 million economic relief payments in the first 100 days of the president&#39;s first term. It has now been 77 days since Biden&#39;s inauguration on January 20.</p><p>The IRS and the Treasury Department have sent out more than 156 million stimulus checks, according to a Wednesday <a href=\"https://www.irs.gov/newsroom/irs-treasury-disburse-25-million-more-economic-impact-payments-under-the-american-rescue-plan\">press release</a>, amounting to roughly $372 billion in fiscal support.</p><p>The fourth batch of checks began processing on Friday and are set to be paid out today. The batch consists of about 25 million payments worth roughly $36 billion, the IRS said. Most of the latest set of payments were sent to Social Security beneficiaries who didn&#39;t file 2020 or 2019 tax returns and didn&#39;t use the IRS&#39; non-filers tool to receive stimulus payments last year.</p><p>More than 3 million checks were sent to Supplemental Security Income recipients, and nearly 85,000 payments were delivered to Railroad Retirement Board beneficiaries, the IRS said.</p><p>Checks began reaching households on March 12, just one day after President Joe Biden <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stimulus-biden-signs-trillion-covid-relief-package-checks-direct-payments-2021-3\">signed the American Rescue Plan Act into law</a>. The president said earlier in his term that he aimed to dole out relief payments, accelerate vaccinations, and reopen schools during his first 100 days in office. The first two goals have been met, and with the majority of school teachers and staff now vaccinated, Biden&#39;s final target is within reach.</p><p>Nearly 24 million of the payments in the latest batch will arrive as direct deposits, with the remainder reaching Americans as paper checks.</p><p>The IRS is still reviewing data from the Department of Veterans Affairs to send payments to people who don&#39;t normally file tax returns. The IRS and Treasury created a non-filers tool earlier in the pandemic to target such populations, but Americans without tax returns on record still face longer waits to receive their relief payments.</p><p>The IRS expects to begin processing VA payments at the end of the week, and recipients can expect to see direct deposits starting April 14.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the The US litigation system costs 1.6% of gross domestic product, which is a percent more than the average country in the Organization for Economic Co-operation and Development, he said.</p><p>&#34;Take 10 small business owners out to lunch and ask them what they need to do to meet local, state and federal regulations, and you will understand the problem.&#34;</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jpmorgan-racial-equity-economy-within-own-walls-2021-3\" data-e2e-name=\"inline-read-more-link\">Inside JPMorgan&#39;s $30 billion push for racial equity in the economy - and within its own walls</a></em></p><p>Business owners must deal with an excessive amount of licensing, paperwork, and employment and insurance laws, which can be crippling and even limit the number of new businesses, he said. </p><p>&#34;Very often local regulations are simply a form of low-level corruption in which bureaucrats are paid to slowly … move … paper … around,&#34; the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jp-morgan-chase-jamie-dimon-speaks-against-georgia-voting-law-2021-3\">long-time CEO said</a>, noting that bad regulation &#34;stifles competition.&#34;</p><p>To solve the problem, Dimon said the country must properly manage and regularly review regulations. </p><p>&#34;Smart regulation includes continual improvement, constant cost-benefit analysis and a review of purpose and objectives, which are reported honestly,&#34; he said, adding that he does indeed want &#34;good regulations and good guardrails.&#34; </p><p>He noted the Federal Aviation Administration as an example of how regulation could change. He said the agency has been unable to adopt new air traffic control technology that would cut flight times by 10 minutes and greenhouse gases by 12%. </p><p>Meanwhile, much of the world, he said, has Dailey)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/52d4662c69beddaa70b245a2?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn23@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-28-235_699d1c9872b0c1a8.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn8@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-38-29-454_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=lMLRIZXBpSk:9MugJK2RNag:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn71@2020_1/2021/04/07/17-38-28-796_24d12c388a1be17c.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=lMLRIZXBpSk:9MugJK2RNag:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn36@2020_1/2021/04/07/17-38-28-472_731c01b23c0492b2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn15@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-27-264_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=lMLRIZXBpSk:9MugJK2RNag:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn79@2020_2/2021/04/07/17-38-29-778_ccac1d29d7cad7f2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/lMLRIZXBpSk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn16@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-38-23-568_e52c0a135fa3db70.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617817067369},{"createdTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:47","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:47","title":"Big tech can't keep our kids safe, so the platforms need to at least make it easier for parents to protect their children online","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/social-media-apps-kids-children-parents-safety-youtube-facebook-instagram-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606dd21630004b0019b26698?format=jpeg\" alt=\"child phone\" height=\"1244\" width=\"2488\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Junior, 7, recovering from COVID-19, plays games on his father&#39;s phone on April 25, 2020 in Stamford, Connecticut.\n<p class=\"copyright\">John Moore/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Social media platforms don&#39;t adequately prioritize online safety for kids - but we&#39;ve been asking the wrong things of them.</li>\n<li>Children face real dangers online, including issues like bullying, sexual predators, and more.</li>\n<li>Big Tech needs to partner with parents to give them greater control over their children&#39;s online worlds.</li>\n<li>Brian Bason is a dad of two and the founder and CEO of Bark Technologies.</li>\n<li>This is an opinion column. The thoughts expressed are those of the author.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The recent announcements from social platforms like TikTok, YouTube, and Instagram about their increased child safety efforts have gotten a lot of attention among parents looking for more ways to help protect their children online. And while these are all positive steps, these efforts will not actually solve the broader problem of keeping kids safe online. Ultimately, the announced measures provide only the illusion of safety.</p><p>We absolutely need social platforms to play a vital role in children&#39;s online safety (reporting CSAM, removing bad actors, providing transparency around their data practices, etc.), but the core problem in the current narrative is the expectation that every social platform can - and will - independently build sufficient tools to actually keep children safe. Parents, rather than Big Tech, ultimately own that responsibility - they just need the access to empower them to do so.</p><h2><strong>Big Tech&#39;s #1 focus will never be on child safety</strong></h2><p>It&#39;s no secret that a large social platform&#39;s primary duty is to drive shareholder value by serving its users ads, accomplished by optimizing for user numbers and engagement metrics. Platforms are inherently disincentivized to expend any significant energy on child safety features that reduce usage from one of the largest groups on their platform. Updates made in the name of child safety are generally of the &#34;check-the-box&#34; variety, because social platforms aren&#39;t nonprofits, and they&#39;re not dedicated to providing safe online spaces for kids.</p><p>Some platforms do offer child-focused versions of their apps designed for younger children (i.e., users to whom they can&#39;t yet serve ads because of the Children&#39;s Online Privacy Protection Act, a law that protects the privacy of kids under 13). For example, Facebook Messenger Kids and the rumored upcoming Instagram for Kids. Putting aside the question of whether we want to encourage more social media usage at younger ages, these types of apps usually work reasonably well for kids six to 10.</p><p>But the kid versions simply aren&#39;t cool for a tween or teen to use, are limited in functionality, and are tied in awkward ways to their parent&#39;s account on that platform. To switch to the adult version of the app, all they have to do is fudge their birth date. With no age verification, they can start exploring the entire app or chatting with strangers.</p><p>Alternatively, some platforms provide &#34;parental controls&#34; for kids using the adult versions of their apps, but in most cases, kids can simply turn them off at any point without their parent&#39;s say-so. And even when enabled, parental controls are inherently blunt instruments, often dramatically limiting the usefulness of the app. While disabling specific features can certainly be useful when a (typically younger) child is solely consuming content, they have little impact on the biggest challenges that kids face once they&#39;ve graduated to using the platforms as tools to communicate with others. </p><h2><strong>The dangers kids face online are real</strong></h2><p>At online safety company Bark, we&#39;ve learned firsthand that when kids are online, the chances that they&#39;ll experience some sort of issue are incredibly likely. In Bark&#39;s <strong>2020 annual report</strong>, we analyzed more than 2.1 billion messages across SMS, email, and 30+ social media and messaging platforms, and we found: </p><ul><li>41.4% of tweens and 66.6% of teens were involved in a self-harm/suicidal situation.</li><li>70.9% of tweens and 87.9% of teens encountered nudity or content of a sexual nature. ● 76.7% of tweens and 82.0% of teens experienced bullying as a bully, victim, or witness. </li></ul><p>And a platform&#39;s parental controls - even if implemented well - would have helped with nearly zero of these. Parental controls simply don&#39;t help when a child is being bullied, pressured to send nude photographs of themselves, expressing suicidal thoughts, or being sent unwanted pornography via a DM/text message. </p><p>Granted, on a small handful of platforms, a parent could use the platform&#39;s built-in parental controls to turn off DMs altogether - but this has the side effect of rendering the app largely useless for older kids, and simply shifting the problematic communication to another platform with less restrictive controls. And, most importantly, this naïve &#34;block-or-allow&#34; approach erects a wall between the child and parent - there&#39;s no feedback loop for the parent to offer support. </p><h2><strong>Putting families in charge of their own data </strong></h2><p>Rates of teen/tween suicide, depression, bullying, and online predation have dramatically risen over the last decade, but parents are facing a massive awareness gap when these issues occur. It is too big a burden on our children to expect them to always know when and how to ask for help (statistically, they overwhelmingly don&#39;t), and history has shown that expecting platforms to independently and proactively implement sufficient tools for parents and kids is not a viable option. </p><p>So what is actually needed? While I certainly encourage platforms to continue to work to offer better tools, the number one thing needed is neither controversial nor difficult for platforms to provide: Let users truly own and access their data. Again, the biggest challenges our kids face - rising teen/tween suicide, mental health issues, online predators, and bullying - are all buried within the <strong>content </strong>of their messages.</p><p>Without the ability to move data out of a platform&#39;s walled garden, caregivers have neither awareness of major issues nor teachable moments to guide their kids with responsible usage of technology. </p><p>Just as we have the ability to choose to send our data to other services (e.g., your biometric data to FitBit, or your financial data to Mint), families need data access to utilize specialized online safety tools to gain the awareness needed to help with situations that kids face online. </p><p>While &#34;data portability&#34; may not sound as powerful as &#34;parental controls,&#34; it is the key to helping parents actually be parents in the digital age. Without it, a parent&#39;s only two options are A) don&#39;t let their kids use tech (i.e., the &#34;don&#39;t ride that bike, you might fall off&#34; approach), or B) give their kids access to an unlimited amount of dangers with zero guidance. </p><p>Ultimately the solution is not to demand more &#34;parental controls&#34; from tech companies who aren&#39;t incentivized to provide them in the first place. It is time for them to empower us to fully protect our children.</p><p><em>Brian Bason is a dad of two and the founder and CEO of Bark Technologies, Inc., an online safety company that helps protect more than 5 million kids across the US.</em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a billionaires. </p><p>That&#39;s according to Forbes, which released its <a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/billionaires/\">annual billionaires list</a> on Tuesday. Forbes found that the world&#39;s wealthiest people, many of whom are recognizable as the top names in the business world, are $5 trillion richer than they were one year ago. </p><p>Here&#39;s how the five richest billionaires fared in 2020: </p><ul><li><strong>Jeff Bezos</strong>, Amazon&#39;s CEO, saw his fortune grow from $113 billion in 2020 to $177 billion in 2021</li><li><strong>Elon Musk</strong>, the CEO of Tesla and SpaceX, saw his net worth rise from $24.6 billion in 2020 to $151 billion in 2021</li><li><strong>Bernard Arnault</strong>, the CEO of LVMH, saw his wealth rise from $76 billion in 2020 to $150 billion in 2021</li><li><strong>Bill Gates</strong>, the cofounder of Microsoft, saw his fortune grow from $98 billion in 2020 to $124 billion in 2021</li><li><strong>Mark Zuckerberg</strong>, Facebook&#39;s CEO, saw his net worth rise from $54.7 billion in 2020 to $97 billion in 2021</li></ul><p>In the case of Bezos, for example, skyrocketing demand for Amazon&#39;s goods and services during the pandemic fueled his wealth gains; for Musk, Tesla&#39;s soaring stock price boosted his fortune to new heights, allowing him to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-jeff-bezos-net-worth-worlds-richest-tesla-amazon-stock-2021-1\">jockey with Bezos</a> for the title of world&#39;s richest person. </p><p>There were also 493 new billionaires forged in the last year, a new one every 17 hours on average, Forbes found. In total, Forbes&#39; list includes 2,755 billionaires. </p><p>These staggering jumps in wealth for the world&#39;s richest came amid a period of economic uncertainty and job losses for millions of people. Between March 2020 and February 2021, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/billionaires-in-america-got-so-much-richer-during-pandemic-2021-3\">80 million Americans lost their jobs</a> - from June to November 2020, roughly 8 million people in the US <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-many-americans-fell-into-poverty-during-pandemic-2020-12\">fell below the poverty line</a>.</p><div src=\"https://i.insider.com/606db97f30004b0019b2660c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Webull vs Robinhood\" height=\"1060\" width=\"2121\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Older retail investors appear to be pushing money back into securities.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Dean Mitchell</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Boomer retail investors are likely behind the weekly rise to $1.2 href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Retail investors are pouring money back into equities and other financial markets, with one data firm saying their faster-than-expected return to weekly purchases appears to be led by buying among Boomers.</p><p>There was a rise to $1.2 billion in average daily purchases of US securities this week, meeting the average for the last 12 months, Vanda Research said Wednesday. The company&#39;s VandaTrack data-analysis arm monitors retail investing activity in 9,000 individual stocks and ETFs in the US.</p><p>The firm about two weeks ago observed that <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/retail-investors-stock-buying-stimulus-underperform-sp-market-2021-3-1030242750\">retail investors had gone into a &#34;hibernation&#34; period</a> after suffering heavy losses in February and underperforming the <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/s&p_500_500\">S&#38;P 500</a>. </p><p>Vanda said Wednesday that data suggest wealthier people from the Boomer generation may have been the driving force by this week&#39;s climb in purchases, resulting in a &#34;sudden comeback&#34; in activity among retail investors.</p><p>&#34;Most of the stocks that made it to the top of our leaderboard this week are high-quality blue chips, while more speculative stocks like GME or AMC have dropped out,&#34; wrote Giacomo Pierantoni, a research analyst at Vanda Research, referencing <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/gme-stock\">GameStop</a> and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/amc-stock\">AMC Entertainment</a>. The video game retailer and the movie theaters operator this year have exploded in popularity, particularly among younger retail investors.</p><p>The increase in blue-chips buying points to behavior by older and more financially conservative investors who are &#34;a lot more wealthy than millennials,&#34; said Vanda, which noted that the average age of investors in platforms like Schwab or TD Ameritrade is close to 50.</p><p>Meanwhile, &#34;unusually large inflows into sovereign bond and credit ETFs,&#34; added to Vanda&#39;s view that Boomers were leading the retail activity. <br><br>&#34;While most Robinhooders tend to stay away from &#39;boring&#39; fixed-income products, Boomers, who are closer to retirement, often prefer them to equities,&#34; said Pierantoni, referring to the Robinhood trading app. He also pointed to monthly data from clients at Charles Schwab that showed inflows into bond ETFs and mutual funds have been twice as large as those into equities. <br><br>More than $416 million last week was pushed into the 30 largest fixed-income ETFs traded in the US, the largest amount on record, said Vanda. The <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/etfs/ishares-iboxx-investment-grade-corporate-bond-etf-us4642872422\">iShares IBoxx $ Investment Grade Corporate Bond ETF</a>  &#34;was the most important contributor&#34; with $128 million purchases, Vanda said.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a
