</strong><strong> </strong></li></ul><bi-shortcode id=\"commerce-link\" class=\"mceNonEditable\" data-cardtype=\"small\" data-pid=\"5e946d4b73d0c853833bac04\" data-purchase-option=\"\">Shipping Charge (small)</bi-shortcode><p><em>This content is intended for readers 21+. Please drink responsibly. If you or anyone you know is dealing with alcohol abuse, get help. The </em><a href=\"https://www.samhsa.gov/find-help/national-helpline\"><em>Substance Abuse and Mental Health Services Administration&#39;s National Helpline</em></a><em> at 1-800-662-HELP (4357) provides a free, confidential, 24/7, treatment referral, and information service.</em></p><p>If buying unique wines at wholesale prices and having them delivered to your doorstep sounds ideal, you should check out <a href=\"https://www.awin1.com/cread.php?awinmid=17197&awinaffid=257137&ued=https%3A%2F%2Fus.nakedwines.com%2FAWINANGELWINANGEL\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Nakedwines.com</a>.</p><p>The 12-year-old company invests in over 150 indie winemakers around the world and uses a lean business model to bring unique, high-end wines to market for cheap.</p><bi-shortcode id=\"related-article-module\" class=\"mceNonEditable\" data-type=\"5a6b8e5c1784254f0f8b4d6d\" data-title=\"The best wine subscriptions in 2021\" data-url=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/best-wine-club\" data-thumbnail=\"https://i.insider.com/5f7f49ecc655f6001969eff8\" data-shortcode-display-text=\"Related Article Module: The best wine subscriptions in 2021\"> </bi-shortcode><p>For shoppers, Nakedwines.com is a relatively inexpensive way to get good, unique wines sent to their door. For winemakers, it&#39;s kind of like a &#34;Shark Tank&#34; for their industry: They propose a wine, it gets approved, and Nakedwines.com gives them an advance to make it happen. Part of how the company has the funds to operate this way is through over 100,000 voluntary &#34;Angel&#34; customers who act as investors.</p><p>Once accepted into the program (and I&#39;d wager every &#34;applicant&#34; is), Angel members invest $40 every month into their Naked Wine piggy bank. This pool of crowdfunded money helps Naked Wine invest in its winemakers, but it&#39;s also never lost to Angel members; the $40 in the virtual piggy bank can be used on their individual wine orders whenever they like - in other words, it&#39;s pretty much like a wine bank account.</p><p>If all goes to plan, it&#39;s good for the company, the consumers, and the winemakers - like <a href=\"https://us.nakedwines.com/producers/carmen-stevens\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener nofollow nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Carmen Stevens</a>, reportedly South Africa&#39;s first black woman to graduate in wine-making (funded by 2,000 Angel members and $200,000 in eight hours).</p><p>To be clear, what you&#39;re getting is not quite a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/best-wine-club\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">wine subscription</a> in the traditional sense. You can just buy wine directly from the site as you would anywhere else (though you need to order six bottles to ship), but the site&#39;s Angel members get special perks. They save 40-60% on all their orders and get a ton of freebies and perks like samples of other wines included in their deliveries, a bottle of Angel-funded wine worth $20 or more each month they order a case of wine, access to Angel-only wines, invites to wine tastings to meet the winemakers, and access to an exclusive priority hotline for any needed support.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5efcb81ef34d05445d262773?format=jpeg\" alt=\"nakedwines.com review\" height=\"3024\" width=\"4032\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Nakedwines.com sells affordable bottles that are what I&#39;d call &#34;easy drinking&#34; wines - perfect for casual drinking.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jada Wong/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>I&#39;d wager most people wind up on the site thanks to a suspiciously generous $100 voucher for new customers - I received mine inside the box of a Bloomingdale&#39;s purchase. Using the voucher, I got a Discovery Case with 12 bottles of wine across a wide spectrum of offerings from the site. With the $100 voucher - which you can also get by <a href=\"https://www.awin1.com/cread.php?awinmid=17197&awinaffid=257137&ued=https%3A%2F%2Fus.nakedwines.com%2FAWIN100FAWIN100\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener nofollow nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">clicking the top right-hand button that says &#34;voucher&#34; and entering your email</a> - the case was $79.99, instead of its current sale price of $179.99 (its traditional cost is listed at $264). This promo varies a bit depending on how many bottles are in the box - my colleague redeemed a $50 voucher for six bottles of wine.</p><p>In-person, the wines are good. I was satisfied and even a little surprised by their quality given the fact that I received $100 off lots of wine. The affordable bottles were what you&#39;d call &#34;easy drinking&#34; wines - none that were bold and weird and revelatory - but perfect for casual drinking. Nakedwines.com hit the &#34;weekday wine&#34; niche perfectly.</p><p>Shipping is also inexpensive. For orders under $100, Nakedwines.com typically charges $10. For orders $100 and more, delivery is free - except for New Jersey, Hawaii, and Alaska, (<a href=\"https://us.nakedwines.com/content/help-faqs.htm\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener nofollow nofollow nofollow sponsored\">you can find rates for these states here</a>). Wines will be delivered in four to seven business days (Monday-Friday or Tuesday-Saturday) during regular business hours, but make sure that there is someone over 21 years old who can sign for the package.</p><p>One thing I would stress is that if you have any difficulty with your shipment, or you don&#39;t like a wine, you should contact Nakedwines.com for help. My experiences with them were as a consumer rather than a reporter, and I was impressed by their easygoing willingness to make sure I had a positive experience, even when it wasn&#39;t to their immediate advantage. This means that if you really hated a wine, they&#39;ll refund you. The site has a &#34;cast-iron, no questions asked, 100% guarantee.&#34;</p><p><a href=\"https://www.awin1.com/cread.php?awinmid=17197&awinaffid=257137&ued=https%3A%2F%2Fus.nakedwines.com%2FAWINANGELWINANGEL\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener nofollow nofollow sponsored\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e754c89671de0445535d414?format=jpeg\" alt=\"naked wines 2\" height=\"749\" width=\"1000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Winemaker Jen Pfeiffer showcasing her Diamond Merlot: rich and complex with plummy mulberry fruit. She recommends it with veggie lasagna or herb crumbed pork schnitzel.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Nakedwines.com/Instagram</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p><p>What makes <a href=\"https://www.awin1.com/cread.php?awinmid=17197&awinaffid=257137&ued=https%3A%2F%2Fus.nakedwines.com%2FAWINANGELWINANGEL\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener nofollow nofollow sponsored\">Nakedwines.com</a> even more appealing is that it&#39;s also pretty social. Winemakers and members interact with each other. Winemakers get feedback directly from customers, and customers can ask them questions. Indirectly, members can rate and recommend wines to each other. </p><p>This communication creates an optional whirlpool of discovery and self-improvement, which is baked into the business from the top down to the granular level of your account; if you don&#39;t like a wine, give it a thumbs down in your Naked Me account. From then on, they&#39;ll help steer you away from wines that taste similar to the ones you didn&#39;t enjoy. Nakedwines.com also uses this as an indirect polling system, helping them determine which winemakers are doing the best job of making wines people really love.</p><h2>The bottom line</h2><p>All in all, Nakedwines.com has good wine for an accessible price, with the opportunity to be as involved as you want to be. It&#39;s also easy to cancel right in your online account if you change your mind as opposed to calling or emailing customer service.</p><p>If you use Naked as a casual wine drinker, you&#39;ll discover great and affordable wines (even if you don&#39;t take advantage of the $100 off coupon) through an interesting system that makes you feel more involved than just ordering another case of wine online. </p><h3><a href=\"https://www.awin1.com/cread.php?awinmid=17197&awinaffid=257137&ued=https%3A%2F%2Fus.nakedwines.com%2FAWIN100FAWIN100\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow nofollow 01:37:47","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:47","title":"How to spot the symptoms of a blood clot","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/blood-clot-symptoms-how-to-spot-clot-and-get-treated-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6034f7a0d920880018591710?format=jpeg\" alt=\"France vaccine AstraZeneca box\" height=\"1333\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A box containing vials of the AstraZeneca Covid-19 vaccine is pictured at the Foch hospital in Suresnes.\n<p class=\"copyright\">ALAIN JOCARD/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Blood clots are a rare but possible side effect of AstraZeneca&#39;s COVID-19 vaccine.</li>\n<li>Clots can cause problems if they block an important vein or artery.</li>\n<li>Symptoms of clots include shortness of breath, swelling, and severe and persistent headaches.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Blood clots are an extremely rare but serious <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/astrazeneca-vaccine-side-effects-blood-clots-very-rare-ema-2021-4\">side effect of AstraZeneca&#39;s COVID-19 vaccine,</a> regulators announced on Wednesday.</p><p>The benefits of AstraZeneca&#39;s vaccine still outweigh the risks, the European Medicines Agency (EMA) said in a <a href=\"https://www.ema.europa.eu/en/news/astrazenecas-covid-19-vaccine-ema-finds-possible-link-very-rare-cases-unusual-blood-clots-low-blood\">press release</a>. Still, the agency&#39;s safety committee said it&#39;s important to know the signs of a possible clot.</p><p>A <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/what-causes-blood-clots\">blood clot</a> occurs when the blood thickens and forms a semi-solid mass. It can be a helpful response to stop bleeding in the case of injury, but these blockages can cause problems if they cut off blood flow to a vital area.</p><p>Blood clots can cause blockages in the legs, abdomen, and lungs. Most of the blood clots associated with the AstraZeneca vaccine have occurred in veins in people&#39;s brains. These clots, known as cerebral venous sinus thrombosis (CVST), can lead to stroke, seizures, and death.</p><p>So far, most of the clots reported have occurred in women under 60 years of age within two weeks of vaccination. Since young people are more likely to experience this side effect, UK vaccine regulators recommend that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/under-30s-shouldnt-take-astrazeneca-vaccine-uk-regulator-2021-4\">people under 30 do not get the AstraZeneca shot</a> unless they&#39;ve already received their first dose.</p><h2><strong>Blood clot symptoms include shortness of breath and headaches</strong></h2><p>The EMA said patients who got the AstraZeneca vaccine should seek medical assistance immediately if they have the following symptoms:</p><ul><li aria-level=\"1\">shortness of breath</li><li aria-level=\"1\">chest pain</li><li aria-level=\"1\">swelling in your leg</li><li aria-level=\"1\">persistent abdominal (belly) pain</li><li aria-level=\"1\">neurological symptoms, including severe and persistent headaches or blurred vision</li></ul><p>Some mild <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-long-it-takes-covid-19-vaccine-to-work-2021-1\">side effects</a>, like pain at the injection site or other body aches, are common in the days post-vaccine. But if you experience severe or persistent symptoms around four to 20 days after vaccination, you should seek medical attention, according to the <a href=\"https://worldhealthorganization.cmail19.com/t/ViewEmail/d/BF096066B984974F2540EF23F30FEDED/D0083294ADD52E090CC2E775D3CF5869\">World Health Organization</a>.</p><p>Blood clots are typically treated with anti-clotting medication. Complications can be avoided if the clot is caught early.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href=\"https://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/10-things-opening-bell?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&#38;utm_medium=ingest\" href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/tcehy-stock\">Tencent&#39;s</a> American ADR sank as much as 9.7% on Wednesday after the firm&#39;s largest shareholder, Prosus, said it plans to sell $14.6 billion worth of its stake in the Chinese multinational technology conglomerate.</p><p>Tencent&#39;s Hong Kong shares fell 3.75% on the day.</p><p>Prosus, the international internet assets division of the South African multinational Naspers, will remain Tencent&#39;s largest shareholder holding some 28.9% of the company.</p><p>Prosus also said it will not sell any more Tencent shares for at least the next three years.</p><p><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/naprf-stock\">Naspers</a><a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/market-data/quotes/NPSNY?mod=chiclets\"> </a>paid $34 million for a 46.5% stake in Tencent in 2001, three years before the company went public in Hong Kong in June 2004.  The acquisition was one of the most lucrative venture capital deals of all time netting Naspers billions.</p><p>Before the latest sale, Naspers, through Prosus, owned a 30.9% stake in Tencent.</p><p>The deal is set to increase Prosus&#39; cash reserves from $4.6 billion to roughly $19.2 billion.</p><p>Tencent is the world&#39;s largest videogame company by revenue and operates the popular WeChat app. The company outperformed in 2020 amid an increased stay-at-home audience for its games and apps during the pandemic.</p><p>Tencent&#39;s stock has made huge strides over the past few years due in large part to its lucrative investments in tech firms like Snapchat, the Chinese e-commerce company Pinduoduo, and the delivery and shopping platform Meituan.</p><p>The company&#39;s ADR, which trades on OTC markets, reached highs of nearly $100 per share on February 12-giving the company a valuation of over $900 billion-but has fallen roughly 20% in the past few months.</p><p>Share prices were hurt by investors&#39; fears of <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/tencent-sheds-65-billion-government-crackdown-ant-group-2021-3-1030203312\">China&#39;s recent crackdown</a> on big tech names. After Wednesday&#39;s fall, Tencent has lost over $150 billion in market cap from its record highs. </p><p>Shares of the company&#39;s ADR traded down 7.38% as of 12:03 p.m. ET after mounting a mild recovery.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606de01a30004b0019b266f8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Tencent chart\" height=\"705\" width=\"827\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p src=\"https://i.insider.com/6063769c6183e1001981958b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"jamie dimon jpmorgan\" height=\"3070\" width=\"4427\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>JPMorgan CEO Jamie Dimon said the US should get rid of tax breaks for horse racing, race cars, and golf courses.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mike Blake/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>JPMorgan CEO Jamie Dimon blasted tax breaks in his annual shareholder letter on Wednesday.</li>\n<li>Dimon proposed major tax reforms to promote growth and address income inequality. </li>\n<li>The comments come as President Biden proposes a corporate tax rate increase.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The chief executive of Wall Street&#39;s biggest bank thinks the US tax code could use a major overhaul. </p><p>In his <a href=\"https://reports.jpmorganchase.com/investor-relations/2020/ar-ceo-letters.htm\">annual letter to shareholders</a> published Wednesday, JPMorgan CEO Jamie Dimon said the country is bogged down by selfishness, self-interest, and sluggish bureaucracy. He specifically called out corporate tax loopholes that he says should have been eliminated long ago. </p><p>&#34;Then there&#39;s our tax code - buried in it are an extraordinary number of loopholes, credits and exemptions that aren&#39;t about competitiveness or good tax policy,&#34; Dimon said. &#34;Private equity, venture capital and real estate still get carried interest, and sugar and cotton, for some unknown reason, still get government subsidies.&#34;</p><p>Carried interest is the part of a private equity firm&#39;s or investment fund&#39;s profits that it uses to pay fund managers. The carried-interest loophole treats that money as capital gains rather than income, meaning it&#39;s taxed at a much lower rate. </p><p>Loopholes in the tax code ultimately end up stymieing competition, according to Dimon. </p><p>&#34;Suffice it to say, industry gets its share of tax breaks and forms of protection from legitimate competition,&#34; he said.</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jpmorgan-ceo-jamie-dimon-remote-work-return-office-shareholder-letter-2021-4\">JPMorgan CEO Jamie Dimon says remote work can undermine the &#39;character&#39; of a company and lays out the bank&#39;s plans for the future of the office</a></em></p><p>Dimon called on lawmakers to create a &#34;proper and consistent tax and fiscal policy&#34; that would drive growth and improve income inequality. The government should have a fiscal policy that&#39;s simple and transparent, and one which allows it to collect all taxes owed, Dimon said. The federal government should also set a target for the amount it aims to collect in taxes over time, he said. </p><p>Dimon recommended raising taxes on the high earners and getting rid of a &#34;maze&#34; of unnecessary tax breaks that primarily benefit the wealthy. Tax breaks for race cars, private jets, and horse racing, along with a land conservation tax break for golf courses, should all be eliminated, Dimon said. </p><p>Democrats and Republicans should set aside partisanship to address what he considers the country&#39;s public policy failures, Dimon said. </p><p>&#34;We must remember that the concepts of free enterprise, rugged individualism and entrepreneurship are not incompatible with meaningful safety nets and the desire to lift up our disadvantaged citizens,&#34; he said. </p><p>Dimon&#39;s comments come as President Joe Biden pitches raising the corporate tax rate from 21% to 28% to finance a sweeping <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-bidens-2-trillion-infrastructure-plan-means-for-you-2021-4\">$2 trillion infrastructure package</a> that would address an array of issues from <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/joe-biden-electric-vehicle-charging-stations-plan-industry-experts-2030-2021-3\">electric-vehicle charging</a> to high-speed internet access. </p><p>The Business Roundtable, a consortium of CEOs of major US firms, <a href=\"https://www.businessroundtable.org/business-roundtable-calls-for-bipartisan-infrastructure-legislation-will-oppose-corporate-tax-increases\">decried</a> the proposed tax hike as creating &#34;new barriers to job creation and economic growth.&#34; But some large corporations - including <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-supports-corporate-tax-hike-biden-infrastructure-plan-bezos-says-2021-4\">Amazon</a> and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/lyft-joins-amazon-support-higher-corporate-taxes-2021-4\">Lyft</a> - have begun to voice their support. </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 07 Apr 2021 14:24:59 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/606db94d30004b0019b2660a?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"0573dbf045623a9de5a94694d5fef118","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn63@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-25-418_1598e62ab221be15.webp","destWidth":1805,"destHeight":1354,"sourceBytes":58142,"destBytes":58142,"author":"insider@insider.com (Jake Lahut)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/606db95c30004b0019b2660b?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn15@2020_2/2021/04/07/17-38-27-725_9b6f5eb0eaef6e39.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn8@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-38-29-454_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=SLT6XScgJjo:6wPcxd7U1ks:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn84@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-38-27-098_8f214f16fcaea0fd.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=SLT6XScgJjo:6wPcxd7U1ks:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn11@2020_5/2021/04/07/17-38-27-644_1490c0a90d8cff96.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn15@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-27-264_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=SLT6XScgJjo:6wPcxd7U1ks:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn24@2020_1/2021/04/07/17-38-26-314_6e5ade0d5038a8da.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/SLT6XScgJjo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn11@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-26-364_2aac628797a72512.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617817067371},{"createdTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:47","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:47","title":"Arkansas faces a Trans Exodus after passing 3 anti-trans bills in 3 weeks","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/arkansas-3-anti-trans-bills-in-3-weeks-triggers-exodus-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606de1a230004b0019b26704?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Trans protest\" height=\"2000\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A protest to support trans people in 2017 in New York City.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Spencer Platt/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The Arkansas state legislature has passed 3 anti-trans bills in less than a month. The latest limits access to medical care.</li>\n<li>Trans people are taking about leaving, but they note that 19 states have taken up similar bills. </li>\n<li>&#34;There&#39;s not going to end up being a lot of places to run to, but a lot of places to run from,&#34; said one trans woman.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Jacqueline Middleton has lived in Arkansas for most of her life, but she plans on moving away from the state as soon as possible now that state lawmakers have pushed through three <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/arkansas-sets-dangerous-precedent-for-trans-youth-in-the-us-2021-3\">anti-trans</a> bills in three weeks. </p><p>But it&#39;s not yet clear where she will go, or how she will manage building a life away from her current support system and everything she has ever known.  </p><p>&#34;It&#39;s heartbreaking,&#34; Middleton told Insider. &#34;It makes me stressed. It&#39;s activating my fight or flight response.&#34; </p><p>The latest blow came on Tuesday, when the state legislature approved a ban on puberty blockers and hormones for trans minors, and cut off  access to any medical care or affirmation from mental health professionals or school employees until they turn 18. </p><p><a href=\"https://www.insider.com/arkansas-vetoes-historic-anti-trans-bill-2021-4\">Gov. Asa Hutchinson</a> vetoed the bill, calling it &#34;a vast government overreach,&#34; but the legislature had enough votes to push it through without him.</p><p>The governor, though, is hardly seen as a trans ally. He previously signed a bill banning trans girls from girl&#39;s scholastic sports, and a sweeping religious exemption for health care providers who can now turn away LGBTQ patients for non-emergencies. </p><p>Middleton, a 23 year old trans woman, transitioned while attending Southern Arkansas University, but had to drop out after several people in the small college town threatened her safety. She&#39;s struggled to find a job since, describing how she&#39;d show up for interviews and employers would realize she&#39;s trans and lose interest. Then, last September, Middleton caught Covid, which led to developing tenosynovitis, an inflammatory disease that affects her wrists and thumbs.</p><p>Now on Medicaid, she worries about losing access to the hormones keeping her dysphoria at bay. HB 1570, the law banning transition care for minors, bans state funds from being used to fund transition care for all trans people. So state funds towards Middleton&#39;s Medicaid will no longer cover the hormones she needs to survive.</p><p>The American Civil Liberties Union has <a href=\"https://twitter.com/ACLU/status/1379511326062546946\">promised</a> to challenge the law in court, but trans people in the state are following the developments with dread. </p><p>For Middleton, the anti-trans health care bill was the last straw.</p><p>&#34;I have to go somewhere where there are people standing behind me and that&#39;s not here,&#34; she said. </p><p>&#34;I would be willing to endure this if it felt like there was any chance that I could overturn it. And if I can&#39;t overturn it here, I&#39;ll go somewhere else.&#34; </p><p>Insider spoke to several trans people living in Arkansas who said they were contemplating a move out of state. </p><p>Last week, while the governor was considering how to respond to the bill cutting off health care for trans kids, Evelyn Rios Stafford, a Justice of the Peace in Fayetteville and Arkansas&#39; only openly trans elected official, said she had a 40-minute meeting to discuss how the measure would impact trans people in the state. </p><p>&#34;Honestly, they&#39;re worried,&#34; she said of what she told the governor. &#34;They don&#39;t know what else is coming down the pipeline.&#34; </p><p>But finding a trans-friendly place to live could prove complicated, given that 19 states have taken up similar bills to the one passed in Arkansas. Middleton has considered Illinois, the nearest state not currently likely to pass new anti-trans laws. </p><p>&#34;It looks like a lot of other states are following suit,&#34; she said. &#34;There&#39;s not going to end up being a lot of places to run to, but a lot of places to run from.&#34;</p><h2>&#34;WHAT ELSE IS COMING?&#34; </h2><p>While the ACLU has led opposition to the anti-trans efforts across the country, in Arkansas, a group called Intransitive has been leading the fight locally. </p><p>&#34;The majority of trans people in the country live in the South,&#34; said Rumba Yambú, the group&#39;s director. &#34;There are a lot of trans people here who have been living, resisting, organizing here for years. We just needed help.&#34;</p><p>According to Rios Stafford, there&#39;s currently no one in the state performing gender reassignment surgery. There is only one clinic, the Gender Spectrum Clinic at Arkansas Children&#39;s Hospital in Little Rock, that serves trans adolescents.</p><p>At the state Senate hearing on the trans health care bill, Dr. Michele Hutchinson, the doctor in charge of the clinic, <a href=\"https://sg001-harmony.sliq.net/00284/Harmony/en/PowerBrowser/PowerBrowserV2/20210322/-1/21395?gefdesc=&startposition=202103221506030603\">testified</a> about the impact the legislature&#39;s work was having on patients. </p><p>&#34;I&#39;m doing everything I can to maintain my sanity here,&#34; Hutchinson <a href=\"https://sg001-harmony.sliq.net/00284/Harmony/en/PowerBrowser/PowerBrowserV2/20210322/-1/21395?gefdesc=&startposition=202103221506030603\">said</a>. </p><p>&#34;Just after this bill passed the House, these kids heard about it. I&#39;ve had multiple kids in our emergency room because of an attempted suicide. Just in the last week,&#34; she <a href=\"https://newrepublic.com/article/161875/arkansas-transgender-law-hormones-doctors-youth\">told legislators</a>.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606dcccf70954f0019195a0d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Trans symbol\" height=\"4174\" width=\"6261\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A rally in support of transgender people at New York City Hall in 2018.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Drew Angerer/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Puberty blockers are widely considered to be standard care for trans adolescents and have been endorsed by every major medical association in the US, including the American Academy of Pediatrics, the American Medical Association, the American Psychological Association, the Endocrine Society, the World Professional Association for Transgender Health, and the American College of Obstetricians and Gynecologists.<strong> </strong></p><p>The only proven treatment for gender dysphoria, the term for a feeling of incongruence between a person&#39;s gender identity and assigned sex at birth, is transitioning. Before puberty, a child has no need for medical interventions, so a transition would be a different haircut, clothes, and maybe a new name and different pronouns.</p><p>It&#39;s not until puberty begins at around 11 or 12 that any sort of medical intervention comes into play. Puberty blockers <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/what-are-puberty-blockers-standard-treatment-transgender-youth-teenagers-2020-12\">are not permanent</a> and help trans kids put off the permanent effects of both their natal puberty, while hormone replacement therapy is typically given to older teens and triggers a puberty consistent with their gender identity. </p><p>The two step approach is meant to put off permanent body development until the person can make a more informed decision about the future. Genital surgery before age 18 is extremely rare. </p><p>&#34;We&#39;ve witnessed overall such a huge rise in the visibility of trans people in this country over the past decade,&#34; said trans historian Jules Gill-Peterson. And yet, she said, there&#39;s a common misperception that the existence of trans kids is a fairly new development. </p><p>While researching her book, &#34;Histories of the Transgender Child,&#34; Gill-Peterson found letters from trans youth to the earliest providers of hormone replacement therapy, in the 1930s, begging for help in stopping their natal pubertal development. </p><p>She realized that has long as there have been trans people, there have also been trans children. And, perhaps more importantly, as long as there has been transition-related care, trans adolescents have sought it out. </p><p>But, while the federal government has expanded access to trans medical care, conservatives on the state level have weaponized the ability of trans individuals to access care and equal rights. </p><p>&#34;It&#39;s clear that right-wing politicians and an array of sort of extremist right-wing groups have been gravitating increasingly towards trans issues, taking advantage of that cultural visibility to try and turn it into a sort of wedge issue,&#34; Gill-Peterson said.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/arkansas-3-anti-trans-bills-in-3-weeks-triggers-exodus-2021-4'>Business Sgt. John Raven</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The Air Force rolled out its new F-15EX fighter Wednesday, officially giving it a name.</li>\n<li>The service is buying at least 144 &#34;Eagle II&#34; jets to replace the ageing fleet of F-15C/Ds.</li>\n<li>The Air Force received its first F-15EX a little over a month after the aircraft&#39;s inaugural flight.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The Air Force officially rolled out its newest fighter jet Wednesday at Eglin Air Force Base in Florida, where the service finally announced its name.</p><p>The F-15EX will be called the &#34;Eagle II,&#34; following in the naming tradition of the F-15C Eagle and F-15E Strike Eagle.</p><p>The Air Force put in its first F-15EX order last July, ordering eight jets. The service plans to obtain at least 144 of these fighters to replace the ageing fleet of C and D variant F-15s.</p><p>The F-15 is an exceptional fighter aircraft, having never been shot down in combat, but the average age of the F-15C/D fleet is almost 40 years old. Around 75% of the fleet is flying past its service life, and 10% of the fighters are grounded due to various structural issues.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/604f7d9287891e0019850cca?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Air Force F-15EX fighter jet\" height=\"1259\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The F-15EX, the Air Force&#39;s newest fighter aircraft, arrives to Eglin Air Force Base in Florida, March 11, 2021.\n<p class=\"copyright\">US Air Force/Samuel King Jr</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Though the Air Force prefers the fifth-generation F-35 Lightning II Joint Strike Fighters, the Pentagon determined that the fourth-generation F-15EX fighters were a much more cost-effective option for quickly modernizing the F-15 fleet to maintain capacity. The Air Force is buying both platforms as replacements for older fighters.</p><p>The new F-15EX is a two-seat aircraft, though it can be flown by a single pilot, that features fly-by-wire controls, advanced avionics, including some electronic warfare upgrades, and digital cockpit displays.</p><p>It also has an increased payload capacity, with the ability to carry up to around 30,000 pounds of air-to-air missiles and air-to-ground munitions. While the F-15 is touted as an air superiority fighter, the military has regularly used this aircraft for ground-attack missions in post-9/11 conflicts.</p><p>The Boeing fighter made its first flight on Feb. 2, 2021 with test pilot Matt Giese in the cockpit. The aircraft took off from Lambert International Airport in St. Louis, Missouri and flew for 90 minutes, <a href=\"https://boeing.mediaroom.com/news-releases-statements?item=130824\">according to the manufacturer</a>.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/604f7d9287891e0019850cc9?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Air Force F-15EX fighter jet\" height=\"939\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The first F-15EX is delivered to its new home at Eglin Air Force Base in Florida, March 11, 2021.\n<p class=\"copyright\">US Air Force/Tech. Sgt. John Raven</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The Air Force <a href=\"https://www.af.mil/News/Article-Display/Article/2534008/air-force-receives-first-f-15ex/\">officially received its first F-15EX fighter from Boeing</a> in Missouri on March 10, a little over two years after the Air Force chief of staff signed the F-15EX Rapid Fielding Requirement Document.</p><p>The first F-15EX fighter was <a href=\"https://www.af.mil/News/Article-Display/Article/2535577/afs-first-f-15ex-arrives-at-eglin-afb/\">then delivered to Eglin Air Force Base in Florida the next day</a>. The aircraft has been going through developmental and operational testing on base.</p><p>Col. Sean Dorey, the Air Force Life Cycle Management Center Fighters and Advanced Aircraft Directorate&#39;s F-15EX program manager, called the receipt fo the first F-15EX a &#34;big moment for the Air Force.&#34;</p><p>&#34;With its large weapons capacity, digital backbone, and open architecture, the F-15EX will be a key element of our tactical fighter fleet and complement 5th-generation assets,&#34; he said. Additionally, &#34;it&#39;s capable of carrying hypersonic weapons, giving it a niche role in future near-peer conflicts.&#34;</p><p>Two F-15EX fighter aircraft are being delivered this year. The remaining six jets in the first lot will be delivered in 2023. Delivery of aircraft in lots two and three will take place in fiscal years 2024 and 2025.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 01:37:47","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:47","title":"A guide to Safe Mode, a troubleshooting method to use when your computer isn't working properly","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-safe-mode","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606b84f3856cd700198a3451?format=jpeg\" alt=\"man using laptop computer at home\" height=\"1249\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Safe Mode launches your computer with minimal functionality so you can troubleshoot issues.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Oliver Rossi/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li aria-level=\"1\">Safe Mode is a basic diagnostic mode for your operating system that starts the computer without most of its drivers and software. </li>\n<li aria-level=\"1\">You can use Safe Mode to solve serious issues like uninstalling incompatible software or malware that&#39;s preventing your computer from running properly. </li>\n<li aria-level=\"1\">Both Windows and Mac computers can be booted into a version of Safe Mode. </li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tech-reference\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong>Visit Insider&#39;s Tech Reference library for more stories</strong></a><strong>.</strong></li>\n</ul><p>If your computer is experiencing serious problems, either due to a software glitch or <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-malware\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">malware</a>, and will not run properly, then you might need to use <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/safe-mode\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Safe Mode</a>.</p><p>Safe Mode is a basic diagnostic and troubleshooting mode that launches the operating system without most of its usual drivers and software. A computer that refuses to start normally because of a catastrophic glitch should be able to start in Safe Mode, where you can attempt to troubleshoot and resolve the problem.</p><p>Both <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/windows\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Windows</a> and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/mac\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Mac</a> computers have their own version of Safe Mode. </p><h2>What happens in Safe Mode</h2><p>Safe Mode is designed to launch your computer with the minimum necessary software to give you access to your operating system, such as Windows or MacOS. That means it starts with a minimal set of services and drivers. For example, you&#39;ll find that when in Safe Mode, your screen resolution is greatly reduced; the full video drivers are bypassed and instead, a simplified VGA driver is used regardless of the screen resolution. </p><p>Most or all networking and file sharing features are disabled in Safe Mode as well. In addition, no startup programs or third-party software is run at startup. The intention is to start the computer with the minimum configuration to give you the best chance of identifying and solving the problem you&#39;re experiencing. </p><p>Despite the limitations, you can get to all settings and control panels, uninstall software, and run most software, such as utilities and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-windows-defender-microsoft-defender-antivirus\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">antivirus programs</a>. </p><h2>How to start your computer in Safe Mode</h2><p>Both <a href=\"https://shop-links.co/1734971899888345705\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow nofollow noopener sponsored sponsored\">Windows</a> and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fbuy-mac%2Fmacbook-pro%2F13-inch\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Mac</a> have their own version of Safe Mode you can invoke if you&#39;re having a serious problem with your computer. </p><p>The method of starting Safe Mode has changed over the years with various versions of Windows. Through Windows 7, you would typically invoke Safe Mode by pressing the F8 key just as your computer starts to boot. In Windows 10, you don&#39;t have to time pressing a function key during startup. Instead, you can start Safe Mode from the Settings app - restart into Safe Mode from the Recovery section. Read our article on <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-boot-in-safe-mode-windows-10\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">how to boot your Windows 10 computer into Safe Mode</a> for more information.</p><p>You can launch your <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fshop%2Fbuy-mac%2Fmacbook-pro%2F13-inch\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Mac</a> into Safe Mode by holding down the Shift key just as you start your computer. Read our article on <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-start-mac-in-safe-mode\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">how to start your Mac computer in Safe Mode</a> for more information.</p><bi-shortcode id=\"related-article-module-end-of-article\" class=\"mceNonEditable\"><a data-type=\"5fac6ac2bf96b936b9303b23\" data-title=\"Ransomware can encrypt your files and force you to pay money  - here's how to avoid ransomware, or deal with an infectiontion\" data-url=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-ransomware\" data-vertical=\"sai\" data-image=\"https://i.insider.com/5fac71d698669500182b5897\">Ransomware can encrypt your files and force you to pay money - here&#39;s how to avoid ransomware, or deal with an infection</a><a data-type=\"60634733266b204c56496bf1\" data-title=\"What is Secure Boot? he told the Unchained podcast.</li><li id=\"recirc\"><strong><a href=\"https://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/10-things-opening-bell?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingeste=markets&#38;utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&#38;utm_medium=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Sign up here for our daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell</a>.</strong></li></ul><p>Billionaire investor Mark Cuban has praised the controversial upgrades to the Ethereum network, saying they should make it more eco-friendly and help the system&#39;s applications &#34;dwarf&#34; bitcoin.</p><p>Speaking on the <a href=\"https://unchainedpodcast.com/mark-cuban-on-why-he-thinks-eth-is-a-better-store-of-value-than-bitcoin/\">Unchained podcast</a>, Dallas Mavericks owner Cuban said the move to a more efficient system will mean &#34;the holdback of the impact on the environment will change immediately.&#34;</p><p>&#34;That is going to give some people a reason to use Ethereum as a store of value over bitcoin, right there.&#34; He predicted that Ethereum and 2 or 3 other blockchains will prove to be the &#34;winners&#34; in a few years&#39; time.</p><p>Ethereum developers are planning to make major changes to the network that will limit transaction fees and start to burn coins, which has <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/ethereum-ether-eth-miners-protests-changes-destroy-coins-crypto-2021-3-1030172884\">angered many miners</a>. The developers intend to eventually move the system to a whole new way of verifying transactions, known as <a href=\"https://academy.binance.com/en/articles/proof-of-stake-explained\">proof of stake</a>.</p><p>&#34;With proof of stake, you&#39;re going to be able to have... a significantly higher multiple in transactions per second, that&#39;s going to improve the utilization and the opportunities to create on Ethereum,&#34; Cuban told Unchained&#39;s Laura Shin.</p><p>The &#34;Shark Tank&#34; star said he was bullish about the Ethereum blockchain because of its numerous uses, including <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-does-nft-mean-crytpo-non-fungible-tokens-art-explained-2021-2#:~:text=Non%2Dfungible%20tokens%20account%20for,of%20Insider%20for%20more%20stories.?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestm=ingest\">non-fungible tokens</a> and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-smart-contracts-can-work-2018-10\">smart contracts</a>, code that can create secure financial agreements without the need for third parties.</p><p>&#34;I think the applications leveraging smart contracts and extensions on Ethereum will dwarf bitcoin,&#34; he said. &#34;That doesn&#39;t mean I&#39;m going to sell my Bitcoin. I&#39;m not. But at the same time, let&#39;s just say I own a lot more Ethereums than I do bitcoins.&#34;</p><p>The Ethereum blockchain&#39;s native cryptocurrency <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/eth-usd\">ether</a> has soared in recent months to more than $2,000, and is up over 1,000% over the last year.</p><p>The network has been central to the boom in non-fungible tokens or NFTs, collectible digital assets that cannot be exchanged with one another for equal value, or broken down into smaller bits.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/crypto-vc-founder-investment-strategy-understanding-defi-for-beginners-pluto-2021-4\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">A crypto founder breaks down how he secured $50 million in assets under management within 3 months of launching a VC firm - and shares how investors should approach understanding the DeFi space</a></em></p><p>Ethereum developers are planning to make major changes to the network to make it more efficient and predictable. The upgrade to Ethereum 2.0 will see the network more to a &#34;proof of stake&#34; system, which analysts say is quicker and more environmentally friendly, but which is likely to be painful for miners.</p><p>Cuban said the changes would add to the appeal of Ethereum relative to the <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/btc-usd\">bitcoin</a> blockchain.</p><p>&#34;Bitcoin, right now, has evolved to be primarily a store value, and it&#39;s very difficult to use it for anything else,&#34; he said. &#34;You really have to work a lot harder on bitcoin than you do on ethereum.&#34;</p><p>He added: &#34;In a few years, I think Ethereum and maybe 2 or 3 other blockchains will have their place, and those will be the winners.&#34;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/mark-cuban-praises-ethereum-network-upgrades-dwarf-bitcoin-ether-eth-2021-4'>Business Insider</a></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/i01_ZFYwrRY\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 07 Apr 2021 14:43:42 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/606d96b230004b0019b265ac?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"020981884e7ef2024b3d9894bda126cb","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn53@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-38-23-966_fce3356383de05d8.webp","destWidth":4565,"destHeight":3423,"sourceBytes":335730,"destBytes":335730,"author":"hrobertson@businessinsider.com (Harry Robertson)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/606d96b730004b0019b265ad?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn80@2020_2/2021/04/07/17-38-28-437_5e68185ff5fd006d.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn8@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-38-29-454_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=i01_ZFYwrRY:Ed58nmxG1dI:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn95@2020_1/2021/04/07/17-38-27-269_cbc16482b961dbe9.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=i01_ZFYwrRY:Ed58nmxG1dI:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn36@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-29-430_3f94e97c80281c12.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn15@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-27-264_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=i01_ZFYwrRY:Ed58nmxG1dI:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn59@2020_5/2021/04/07/17-38-25-890_7aa5a64ce4c250e1.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/i01_ZFYwrRY":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn99@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-25-805_9ad77c3e6fdb6bc7.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617817067372},{"createdTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:47","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:47","title":"Checking in on your friends and coworkers isn't enough - here are steps you can take at work to help fight racial discrimination","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/fight-racism-mental-health-check-ins-coworkers-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606cc0fa70954f0019195825?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Stop Asian Hate Women\" height=\"2666\" width=\"3555\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A stop Asian hate rally following the violence in Atlanta, Georgia, on March 16, 2021.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Zhao Gang/Xinhua</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Diksha Kale is a criminal defense attorney who researches gender studies and criminal law.</li>\n<li>She says it&#39;s important to do more than just mental health check-ins on your friends during violent times.</li>\n<li>Take action by demanding better policies and donating to or volunteering at organizations working on the ground. </li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Recently, my friend and I were talking over the phone about <a href=\"https://www.latimes.com/california/story/2021-03-26/racist-attacks-inspire-asian-americans-to-fight-back\">the anti-Asian violence that has been taking place in the United States</a>. As a first-generation Filipino Canadian woman, my friend was particularly worried for elders and women in her community who are seen as <a href=\"https://www.nbcnews.com/news/asian-america/there-were-3-800-anti-asian-racist-incidents-mostly-against-n1261257\">easy targets for violent racist attacks</a>.</p><p>But that&#39;s not the only thing she was worried about:</p><p><em>&#34;I am dreading the messages and phone calls that are bound to come in any minute. The mental health check-ins, asking me if I am OK after what happened in Atlanta. I mean the violence did affect me as a person, but it did not affect me personally.&#34;</em></p><p>She went on to explain how her coworker, who happened to be a Black Canadian woman, had received similar check-in messages and calls after what happened to <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/article/breonna-taylor-police.html\">Breonna Taylor</a> and <a href=\"https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-52861726\">George Floyd</a>.</p><p>People who she had gone to school with, people she had not talked to in years were sending messages asking if she was OK. And while <a href=\"https://idontmind.com/journal/just-checking-in-ten-minutes-ten-questions\">we both agree that mental health check-ins are important</a>, there have to be other things people can do to be responsible citizens.</p><p>As a researcher engaged in work related to gender studies and criminal law, with an interest in governance and regulation, I wonder how mental health discourses are employed in the aftermath of racist violence.</p><h2>An exercise in governmentality</h2><p>These mental health check-ins are an exercise in <a href=\"https://criticallegalthinking.com/2014/12/02/governmentality-notes-thought-michel-foucault/\">governmentality</a>. Governmentality is what French philosopher <a href=\"https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/The-Foucault-Effect%3A-Studies-in-Governmentality-Burchell-Gordon/c2322f53910e4fb9eba57a6c2232fc0f493edae5?p2df\">Michel Foucault compared to the &#34;art of government&#34;</a>: it acknowledges that governance is not limited to the acts or decisions of a government alone, and that as a population, we govern each other as well.</p><p>An example of governmentality can be something as mundane as a professional dress code. If you were to show up at a formal event wearing ripped jeans and a tank top, other guests would likely give you a disapproving look. And while you have not broken the law, you have broken some code of conduct. It would not come as a surprise if you were asked to change into formal wear and come back.</p><p>There are three things that happened in the above example: there are rules you must follow; if you don&#39;t follow the rules, you have done something wrong; the people who follow the rules are keeping you in line by ensuring you do as they do.</p><p>These elements can be applied to mental health check-ins as well.</p><h2>Governmentality and mental health check-ins</h2><p>As a South Asian woman, I can put myself in the shoes of a well-meaning ally and check in on my friends. I have seen the <a href=\"https://www.latimes.com/entertainment-arts/story/2021-03-17/atlanta-shooting-stop-asian-hate-celebrity-reactions\">numerous posts on social media</a> about how we <em>must</em> do mental health check-ins.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">-Lana Condor  (@lanacondor) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1372063887554539524?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">March 17, 2021</a></blockquote><script async=\"\" src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>So I listen, scroll through my contacts, friend lists and send <em>the</em> text:</p><p><em>&#34;Hey, I heard about what happened in Atlanta. I am so sorry. If you need to talk to someone about it, I&#39;m here, OK?&#34;</em></p><p>My work as a good ally is done, I go about my day with a sense of accomplishment - but should I?</p><p>This is governance. We do what we tell each other we are <em>supposed</em> to do. And this is where most people think their work as a good ally and responsible citizen is over, but it isn&#39;t.</p><h2>Striking a balance between mental health and justice</h2><p>The US, like many colonial-era countries, has a long <a href=\"https://news.harvard.edu/gazette/story/2021/03/a-long-history-of-bigotry-against-asian-americans/\">history of racial violence against Asian people</a>. The <a href=\"https://www.nbcnews.com/news/asian-america/politicians-businesses-advocates-speak-out-virtual-stopasianhate-day-n1262193\">#StopAsianHate movement</a> is about more than a mass shooting; it is about demanding accountability in the face of white supremacy and hatred.</p><p>Thanks to political leaders like former US president Donald Trump, who <a href=\"https://abcnews.go.com/Health/trumps-chinese-virus-tweet-helped-lead-rise-racist/story?id=76530148\">racialized COVID-19</a>, Asian people have been attacked, abused, and murdered. The <a href=\"https://www.wbur.org/hereandnow/2021/03/22/objectifying-asian-women-racism\">objectification of Asian women</a> in entertainment media has also contributed to the anti-Asian violence we&#39;re witnessing today.</p><p>Studies suggest that <a href=\"https://doi.org/10.1080/713667453\">poor mental health among racial minorities is closely linked with their negative experiences related to racism</a>. Saying that we need to talk about mental health without addressing systemic racism and white supremacy is futile.</p><h2>Check in and demand better</h2><p>So what can one do if mental health check-ins are not enough?</p><p>Agitate and demand better policies. Facilitate healing for Asian communities without interjecting yourself in the process. Donate to, or volunteer with <a href=\"https://www.harpersbazaar.com/culture/politics/a35862857/stop-asian-hate-organizations-to-support/\">organizations that are working on the ground</a> to help those affected.</p><p>Keeping in mind that you can always do more, do check in with your Asian friends. Because mental health is important, and so is justice.<!-- Below is The Conversation's page counter tag. Please DO NOT REMOVE. --><!-- End of code. If you don't see any code above, please get new code from the Advanced tab after you click the republish button. The page counter does not collect any personal data. More info: https://theconversation.com/republishing-guidelines --></p><p><em><a href=\"https://theconversation.com/profiles/diksha-kale-1220214\">Diksha Kale</a>, PhD candidate (Legal Studies), <a (Tercius Bufete)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f7749c80ab50d00184add67?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn79@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-28-903_fb7d8f07a40e2f53.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn8@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-38-29-454_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=rPDP7zNrODs:NbOWLNyO_Qs:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn86@2020_5/2021/04/07/17-38-23-621_91e4386b850df706.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=rPDP7zNrODs:NbOWLNyO_Qs:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn20@2020_2/2021/04/07/17-38-29-468_1f1fa6a1cd6da1a2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn15@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-27-264_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=rPDP7zNrODs:NbOWLNyO_Qs:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn3@2020_6/2021/04/07/17-38-23-629_46707439761200e8.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/rPDP7zNrODs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn83@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-26-240_7529b5a53e79e9c6.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617817067363},{"createdTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:47","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:37:47","title":"Modem vs. router: The differences between the pieces of hardware that connect you to the internet, explained","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/modem-vs-router","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606b5a37856cd700198a3363?format=jpeg\" alt=\"internet router modem\" height=\"1249\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Though they can be combined into one device, modems and routers serve different purposes.\n<p class=\"copyright\">CASEZY/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li aria-level=\"1\">A modem and router work in tandem to deliver you an internet connection.</li>\n<li aria-level=\"1\">Even if the modem and router are combined in the same hardware, they serve distinct functions.</li>\n<li aria-level=\"1\">The modem communicates with the internet service provider to get you access to the internet; the router acts as a management tool for your local area network.</li>\n<li aria-level=\"1\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tech-reference\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Visit Insider&#39;s Tech Reference library for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Your <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/modem\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">modem</a> and your <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/router\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">router</a> may be similar in appearance, but they have distinct roles when it comes to delivering you an internet connection.</p><p>Even if you aren&#39;t running your own server, it&#39;s a good idea to have a basic grasp of how these two pieces of hardware work in tandem to deliver your internet. That way, you&#39;ll have an easier time determining the best router and modem setup for your local network, and troubleshooting any internet-related issues that may arise.</p><p>Here&#39;s a brief explainer on what you should know about your modem and router to keep them running optimally.</p><h2>Modem vs. router</h2><p>The essential difference between a modem and a router is that a modem connects you to the internet as a whole while the router manages and routes the internet to your devices.</p><h3>A modem is your gateway to internet access</h3><p>The modem authenticates and connects you to your chosen internet service provider (ISP), which might be a local provider or a national company like AT&#38;T or Comcast.</p><p>Generally, a <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B077BL65HS/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&tag=bitht_040521_modem-vs-router-20&camp=1789&creative=9325&linkCode=as2&creativeASIN=B077BL65HS&linkId=6b262ed1786ec83939cebf5dfee47320786ec83939cebf5dfee47320\" rel=\"nofollow sponsored\">modem</a> is black, with an appearance similar to a gaming console - flashing lights and a sleek, compact design. They can be as small as a smartphone or as large as a box of cereal. </p><p>The main thing you&#39;ll be concerned with as far as your modem though is its reliability and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-fast-is-my-internet\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">speed connecting to the internet</a>.</p><p>Even if you have the newest, fastest type of modem, factors beyond your control can impact its connection. For instance, old or damaged cable lines that connect your modem to the ISP can cause slower speeds. But that&#39;s something your ISP is on the hook to fix, not you.</p><p>Another issue that can impact modem connectivity is provider availability. For instance, if you don&#39;t have access to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fiber-optic\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">fiber internet</a> or <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-5g\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">5G</a>, it won&#39;t matter that your modem is top-notch. The modem will still be limited in its speed, and depending on the type of modem, may not even work at all.</p><p>There are also two important acronyms to know related to your modem: the ISP and IP address.</p><p>Your ISP, or internet service provider, is the company you&#39;re likely paying to get internet service. Your modem would be a hunk of useless hardware without the ISP to communicate with it.</p><p>If you&#39;ve ever received a copyright-related correspondence from your ISP, that&#39;s because of your ISP&#39;s knowledge of your computer&#39;s IP address: The ISP, using the modem, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-find-ip-address-of-router\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">assigns an IP address to your device</a> when you connect to the network.</p><h3><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B07YMFZ28Q/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&tag=biipgf_091217_best-routers-20&camp=1789&creative=9325&linkCode=as2&creativeASIN=B07YMFZ28Q&linkId=1bbcb4506129d21511f7bec84474faa46129d21511f7bec84474faa4\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Routers</a> give multiple devices access to the internet </h3><p>A router will look similar to the modem: generally boxy and black, though some will have antennas to help broadcast a Wi-Fi signal. </p><p>In fact, both the router and modem might even be occupying the same piece of hardware. Yet they are still distinct devices with distinct functions.</p><p>While the modem provides the essential pipeline to the larger internet, the router acts as a sort of bouncer, manager, and traffic director for your local network. The router is a secure check point that routes internet to your devices as they simultaneously use the internet. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606b5678856cd700198a3340?format=jpeg\" alt=\"internet modem and router\" height=\"1662\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Your modem and router work together to connect you to the internet through your internet service provider, or ISP.\n<p class=\"copyright\">bedo/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>One big factor that may affect the router&#39;s connectivity is if your device is wired or wireless. Wireless networks tend to suffer from disruptions related to the proximity between your devices and the router. </p><p>A few of the most ubiquitous router brands are Netgear and Linksys. Whichever brand you elect to use, your router will be the brains behind your local area network (LAN), routing all the traffic and assigning local IP addresses to any device that&#39;s using your internet.</p><h3>Modems and routers can be stored in one device</h3><p>Sometimes, you&#39;ll see one piece of hardware that houses both the modem and the router. If that&#39;s the case, the hardware is usually provided by your ISP. </p><p>There are some benefits to the two-in-one model. For starters, it&#39;s more compact and easier to set up for novice users.</p><p>However, the benefits of two separate components have an advantage over the convenience of a combo system. With a separate router and modem, there&#39;s more opportunity for hardware upgrades, and also better access to network ports, which are particularly handy if you want to hardwire your connection with an <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-an-ethernet-cable\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Ethernet cable</a>.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/603fd38fb46d720018b04a17?format=jpeg\" alt=\"ethernet cable connected to laptop internet\" height=\"1667\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Connecting to the internet via an Ethernet cable will typically give you a faster connection than Wi-Fi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Chalongrat Chuvaree / EyeEm/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Having your router be separate from your modem also allows you to locate the router in its most ideal location for optimal wireless coverage. </p><p>And technically you don&#39;t even have to have a router - you can bypass a router in favor of plugging directly into the modem with an Ethernet cable. However, the practice would be more inconvenient than Wi-Fi. </p><h2>A mesh network doesn&#39;t replace the need for a router and modem</h2><p>You may have also heard of a &#34;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-mesh-wifi\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">mesh network</a>&#34; when looking into how to best wire your home.</p><p>However, a <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B07WNY2WKG/ref=as_li_tl?ots=1&slotNum=5&imprToken=18bc51db-4079-8b8a-579&ie=UTF8&tag=biipgf_091217_best-routers-20&camp=1789&creative=9325&linkCode=as2&creativeASIN=B07WNY2WKG&linkId=098ca6304d4f187fff1b60e34f8640f0kId=098ca6304d4f187fff1b60e34f8640f0\" rel=\"nofollow sponsored\">mesh network</a> is not to be confused with being a total substitute for a modem-router connection. Instead, a mesh network is a way to extend the reach of your wireless router. </p><p>Even with a device like the Google Wi-Fi system, which essentially does replace the traditional router in favor of mesh, you&#39;ll still ultimately need an ISP and a modem.</p><h2>Buying your own modem and router might be worth it </h2><p>There are a few factors to consider when it comes to whether or not to buy your own router and modem hardware, or &#34;rent&#34; the hardware from your ISP - and often, it is a rental agreement and not an outright purchase.</p><p>Obviously, you may save money over time by investing in your own hardware. However, there&#39;s no guarantee that the available internet service providers will be compatible with the hardware you own.</p><p>On the other hand, renting the modem and/or router means an additional monthly fee, and you also have the hassle of returning the hardware when your contract with the ISP ends.</p><h2>Ways to troubleshoot problems with the modem or router</h2><p>The most common catch-all fix for a range of modem issues, like glitches in the modem&#39;s firmware or other software malfunctions, is &#34;power cycling&#34; - which means turning your modem off and on again. The same fix applies to the router.</p><p>The next best <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/why-isnt-my-internet-working\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">troubleshooting method</a> is checking the cables. You&#39;ll want to make sure the Ethernet cable and power adapters are properly connected. </p><p>Other troubleshooting methods include repositioning your router to eliminate dead Wi-Fi spots in your residence, updating your firmware, and changing your <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-a-network-security-key\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">network security key</a> in case your connection has been accessed by someone else. </p><bi-shortcode id=\"commerce-link\" class=\"mceNonEditable\" data-cardtype=\"small\" data-pid=\"606b77b23d35010018fe113e\" data-purchase-option=\"\">MB7621 Modem (small)</bi-shortcode><bi-shortcode id=\"commerce-link\" class=\"mceNonEditable\" data-cardtype=\"small\" data-pid=\"604be9a3eeecfe0012687ca9\" data-purchase-option=\"\">Archer AX50 (small)</bi-shortcode><bi-shortcode id=\"commerce-link\" class=\"mceNonEditable\" data-cardtype=\"small\" data-pid=\"5f5149bf253b70016c675af8\" data-purchase-option=\"\">Orbi AX6000 Tri-band Mesh WiFi 6 System (2-Pack) (small)</bi-shortcode><bi-shortcode id=\"related-article-module-end-of-article\" class=\"mceNonEditable\"><a data-type=\"603fce25fec9aa70ba417682\" data-title=\"Is Ethernet faster than Wi-Fi? src=\"https://i.insider.com/6038574c05ddb100195f6545?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Jamie Dimon\" height=\"1331\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\"> \n  <figcaption>\n   JPMorgan Chase CEO Jamie Dimon. \n   <p class=\"copyright\">Photo by SAUL LOEB/AFP via Getty Images</p> \n  </figcaption> </img>\n</figure>\n<ul class=\"summary-list\"> \n <li>JPMorgan CEO Jamie Dimon isn't planning a full office when his company ends remote work.</li> \n <li>\"For every 100 employees, we may need seats for only 60 on average,\" he said in a letter to investors.</li> \n <li>As a result, Dimon said, \"This will significantly reduce our need for real estate.\"</li> \n <li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit the Business section of Insider for more stories</a>.</li> \n</ul>\n<p>When JPMorgan Chase employees return to the office, it's likely to look a lot more empty than it did before the pandemic.</p>\n<p>That's because America's largest bank is making drastic changes to its office layout and capacity, CEO Jamie Dimon said <a href=\"https://reports.jpmorganchase.com/investor-relations/2020/ar-ceo-letters.htm\">in his annual letter</a>. </p>\n<p>\"We will quickly move to a more 'open seating' arrangement, in which digital tools will help manage seating arrangements, as well as needed amenities, such as conference room space,\" Dimon said. \"As a result, for every 100 employees, we may need seats for only 60 on average.\"</p>\n<p>As a result, the banking giant is expecting a major reduction in required office real estate (though it remains committed to a new Manhattan headquarters that's in the works for <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/us-jpmorgan-results-realestate/jpmorgan-sticks-with-plan-to-build-giant-new-york-headquarters-idUSKBN26Y2HP\">2024</a>).</p>\n<p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/goldman-sachs-marcus-burnout-cloud-tech-hiring-attrition-culture-gs-2021-4\" data-e2e-name=\"inline-read-more-link\">Burnout, blown deadlines, and a tech talent exodus: How Goldman Sachs' Marcus is struggling to live up to its lofty consumer banking ambitions</a></em></p>\n<p>That doesn't mean the company is embracing remote work in the long term: Just 10% of the bank's roughly 250,000 worldwide employees are expected to work remote on a full-time basis, Dimon said.</p>\n<p>Most employees will still work in an office or banking branch location on a full time basis, with some employees \"working under a hybrid model\" - a mix of remote and in-office work.</p>\n<p>Dimon highlighted the struggles his company has faced across the last year with so many employees working remote: From difficulty onboarding new employees to a lack of \"spontaneous learning and creativity\" that comes from interacting with other people in person.</p>\n<p>JPMorgan was <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/coronavirus-jpmorgan-employees-work-from-home-contingency-plan-test-report-2020-3\">among the first companies to test remote work</a> as reports of coronavirus spreading in the US began in early 2020. The company initially sent home just 10% of its workforce before the onset of the pandemic forced companies and schools to go fully remote.</p>\n<p><em><strong>Got a tip?</strong> Contact Insider senior correspondent Ben Gilbert via email (<a href=\"mailto:bgilbert@insider.com\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\">bgilbert@insider.com</a>),</em><em> or Twitter DM (<a href=\"https://twitter.com/RealBenGilbert\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\">@realbengilbert</a>).
